[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/British_War_Cabinet_Minutes_approving_the_release_of_the_Balfour_Declaration.png/220px-British_War_Cabinet_Minutes_approving_the_release_of_the_Balfour_Declaration.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:British_War_Cabinet_Minutes_approving_the_release_of_the_Balfour_Declaration.png)

British War Cabinet minutes approving the release of the declaration, 31 October 1917

Excerpts from the minutes of these four War Cabinet meetings provide a description of the primary factors that the ministers considered:

-   **3 September 1917**: "With reference to a suggestion that the matter might be postponed, \[Balfour\] pointed out that this was a question on which the Foreign Office had been very strongly pressed for a long time past. There was a very strong and enthusiastic organisation, more particularly in the United States, who were zealous in this matter, and his belief was that it would be of most substantial assistance to the Allies to have the earnestness and enthusiasm of these people enlisted on our side. To do nothing was to risk a direct breach with them, and it was necessary to face this situation."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHurewitz1979103_182-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHurewitz1979103-182">[144]</a></sup>
-   **4 October 1917**: "... \[Balfour\] stated that the German Government were making great efforts to capture the sympathy of the Zionist Movement. This Movement, though opposed by a number of wealthy Jews in this country, had behind it the support of a majority of Jews, at all events in Russia and America, and possibly in other countries ... Mr. Balfour then read a very sympathetic [declaration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cambon_letter "Cambon letter") by the French Government which had been conveyed to the Zionists, and he stated that he knew that President Wilson was extremely favourable to the Movement."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHurewitz1979104_183-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHurewitz1979104-183">[145]</a></sup>
-   **25 October 1917**: "... the Secretary mentioned that he was being pressed by the Foreign Office to bring forward the question of Zionism, an early settlement of which was regarded as of great importance."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHurewitz1979105_184-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHurewitz1979105-184">[146]</a></sup>
-   **31 October 1917**: "\[Balfour\] stated that he gathered that everyone was now agreed that, from a purely diplomatic and political point of view, it was desirable that some declaration favourable to the aspirations of the Jewish nationalists should now be made. The vast majority of Jews in Russia and America, as, indeed, all over the world, now appeared to be favourable to Zionism. If we could make a declaration favourable to such an ideal, we should be able to carry on extremely useful propaganda both in Russia and America."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHurewitz1979106_185-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHurewitz1979106-185">[147]</a></sup>

## Drafting

Declassification of British government archives has allowed scholars to piece together the choreography of the drafting of the declaration; in his widely cited 1961 book, [Leonard Stein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leonard_Stein_(Liberal_politician) "Leonard Stein (Liberal politician)") published four previous drafts of the declaration.<sup id="cite_ref-Stein664_186-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-Stein664-186">[148]</a></sup>

The drafting began with Weizmann's guidance to the Zionist drafting team on its objectives in a letter dated 20 June 1917, one day following his meeting with Rothschild and Balfour. He proposed that the declaration from the British government should state: "its conviction, its desire or its intention to support Zionist aims for the creation of a Jewish national home in Palestine; no reference must be made I think to the question of the Suzerain Power because that would land the British into difficulties with the French; it must be a Zionist declaration."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGutwein2016117–152_118-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGutwein2016117%E2%80%93152-118">[92]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELieshout2016219_187-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTELieshout2016219-187">[149]</a></sup>

A month after the receipt of the much-reduced 12 July draft from Rothschild, Balfour proposed a number of mainly technical amendments.<sup id="cite_ref-Stein664_186-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-Stein664-186">[148]</a></sup> The two subsequent drafts included much more substantial amendments: the first in a late August draft by [Lord Milner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alfred_Milner "Alfred Milner") – one of the original five members of Lloyd George's War Cabinet as a [minister without portfolio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minister_without_portfolio_(United_Kingdom) "Minister without portfolio (United Kingdom)")<sup id="cite_ref-188"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-188">[xvii]</a></sup> – which reduced the geographic scope from all of Palestine to "in Palestine", and the second from Milner and Amery in early October, which added the two "safeguard clauses".<sup id="cite_ref-Stein664_186-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-Stein664-186">[148]</a></sup>

| List of known drafts of the Balfour Declaration, showing changes between each draft |
| --- |

Subsequent authors have debated who the "primary author" really was. In his posthumously published 1981 book _[The Anglo-American Establishment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Anglo-American_Establishment "The Anglo-American Establishment")_, [Georgetown University](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georgetown_University "Georgetown University") history professor [Carroll Quigley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carroll_Quigley "Carroll Quigley") explained his view that Lord Milner was the primary author of the declaration,<sup id="cite_ref-192"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-192">[xviii]</a></sup> and more recently, [William D. Rubinstein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_D._Rubinstein "William D. Rubinstein"), Professor of Modern History at [Aberystwyth University](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aberystwyth_University "Aberystwyth University"), Wales, proposed Amery instead.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERubinstein2000175–196_193-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTERubinstein2000175%E2%80%93196-193">[153]</a></sup> Huneidi wrote that Ormsby-Gore, in a report he prepared for Shuckburgh, claimed authorship, together with Amery, of the final draft form.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHuneidi199833_194-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuneidi199833-194">[154]</a></sup>

## Key issues

The agreed version of the declaration, a single sentence of just 67 words,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECaplan201162_195-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTECaplan201162-195">[155]</a></sup> was sent on 2 November 1917 in a short letter from Balfour to Walter Rothschild, for transmission to the Zionist Federation of Great Britain and Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGelvin201482''ff''_196-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGelvin201482''ff''-196">[156]</a></sup> The declaration contained four [clauses](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clause "Clause"), of which the first two promised to support "the establishment in Palestine of a national home for the Jewish people", followed by two "safeguard clauses"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKattan200960–61_197-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKattan200960%E2%80%9361-197">[157]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBassiouniFisher2012431_198-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBassiouniFisher2012431-198">[158]</a></sup> with respect to "the civil and religious rights of existing non-Jewish communities in Palestine", and "the rights and political status enjoyed by Jews in any other country".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGelvin201482''ff''_196-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGelvin201482''ff''-196">[156]</a></sup>

### The "national home for the Jewish people" vs. Jewish state

> "This is a very carefully worded document and but for the somewhat vague phrase 'A National Home for the Jewish People' might be considered sufficiently unalarming ... But the vagueness of the phrase cited has been a cause of trouble from the commencement. Various persons in high positions have used language of the loosest kind calculated to convey a very different impression to the more moderate interpretation which can be put upon the words. President Wilson brushed away all doubts as to what was intended from his point of view when, in March 1919, he said to the Jewish leaders in America, 'I am moreover persuaded that the allied nations, with the fullest concurrence of our own Government and people are agreed that in Palestine shall be laid the foundations of a Jewish Commonwealth.'<sup id="cite_ref-200"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-200">[w]</a></sup> The late [President Roosevelt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt "Theodore Roosevelt") declared that one of the Allies peace conditions should be that 'Palestine must be made a Jewish State.' Mr. [Winston Churchill](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Winston_Churchill "Winston Churchill") has spoken of a 'Jewish State' and Mr. [Bonar Law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bonar_Law "Bonar Law") has talked in Parliament of 'restoring Palestine to the Jews'."<sup id="cite_ref-201"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-201">[160]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-203"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-203">[x]</a></sup>

Report of the [Palin Commission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palin_Commission "Palin Commission"), August 1920<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalin_Commission19209_204-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalin_Commission19209-204">[162]</a></sup>

The term "national home" was intentionally ambiguous,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMakovsky200776_205-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMakovsky200776-205">[163]</a></sup> having no legal value or precedent in international law,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGelvin201482''ff''_196-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGelvin201482''ff''-196">[156]</a></sup> such that its meaning was unclear when compared to other terms such as "state".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGelvin201482''ff''_196-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGelvin201482''ff''-196">[156]</a></sup> The term was intentionally used instead of "state" because of opposition to the Zionist program within the British Cabinet.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGelvin201482''ff''_196-4"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGelvin201482''ff''-196">[156]</a></sup> According to historian Norman Rose, the chief architects of the declaration contemplated that a [Jewish State](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_State "Jewish State") would emerge in time while the [Palestine Royal Commission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestine_Royal_Commission "Palestine Royal Commission") concluded that the wording was "the outcome of a compromise between those Ministers who contemplated the ultimate establishment of a Jewish State and those who did not."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalestine_Royal_Commission193724_206-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalestine_Royal_Commission193724-206">[164]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Rose1_208-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-Rose1-208">[xix]</a></sup>

Interpretation of the wording has been sought in the correspondence leading to the final version of the declaration. An official report to the War Cabinet sent by Sykes on 22 September said that the Zionists did _not_ want "to set up a Jewish Republic or any other form of state in Palestine or in any part of Palestine" but rather preferred some form of protectorate as provided in the Palestine Mandate.<sup id="cite_ref-210"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-210">[y]</a></sup> A month later, Curzon produced a memorandum<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECurzon1917_211-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTECurzon1917-211">[167]</a></sup> circulated on 26 October 1917 where he addressed two questions, the first concerning the meaning of the phrase "a National Home for the Jewish race in Palestine"; he noted that there were different opinions ranging from a fully fledged state to a merely spiritual centre for the Jews.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELieshout2016225–257_212-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTELieshout2016225%E2%80%93257-212">[168]</a></sup>

Sections of the British press assumed that a Jewish state was intended even before the Declaration was finalized.<sup id="cite_ref-214"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-214">[xx]</a></sup> In the United States the press began using the terms "Jewish National Home", "Jewish State", "Jewish republic" and "Jewish Commonwealth" interchangeably.<sup id="cite_ref-215"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-215">[170]</a></sup>

Treaty expert [David Hunter Miller](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Hunter_Miller "David Hunter Miller"), who was at the conference and subsequently compiled a 22 volume compendium of documents, provides a report of the Intelligence Section of the American Delegation to the [Paris Peace Conference of 1919](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paris_Peace_Conference_of_1919 "Paris Peace Conference of 1919") which recommended that "there be established a separate state in Palestine," and that "it will be the policy of the [League of Nations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/League_of_Nations "League of Nations") to recognize Palestine as a Jewish state, as soon as it is a Jewish state in fact."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedman1973313_216-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedman1973313-216">[171]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Miller_217-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-Miller-217">[172]</a></sup> The report further advised that an independent Palestinian state under a [British League of Nations mandate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mandate_for_Palestine "Mandate for Palestine") be created. Jewish settlement would be allowed and encouraged in this state and this state's holy sites would be under the control of the League of Nations.<sup id="cite_ref-Miller_217-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-Miller-217">[172]</a></sup> Indeed, [the Inquiry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Inquiry "The Inquiry") spoke positively about the possibility of a Jewish state eventually being created in Palestine if the necessary demographics for this were to exist.<sup id="cite_ref-Miller_217-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-Miller-217">[172]</a></sup>

Historian Matthew Jacobs later wrote that the US approach was hampered by the "general absence of specialist knowledge about the region" and that "like much of the Inquiry's work on the Middle East, the reports on Palestine were deeply flawed" and "presupposed a particular outcome of the conflict". He quotes Miller, writing about one report on the history and impact of Zionism, "absolutely inadequate from any standpoint and must be regarded as nothing more than material for a future report".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJacobs2011191_218-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJacobs2011191-218">[173]</a></sup>

[Lord Robert Cecil](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lord_Robert_Cecil "Lord Robert Cecil") on 2 December 1917, assured an audience that the government fully intended that "Judea \[was\] for the Jews."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedman1973313_216-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedman1973313-216">[171]</a></sup> Yair Auron opines that Cecil, then a deputy Foreign Secretary representing the British Government at a celebratory gathering of the English Zionist Federation, "possibly went beyond his official brief" in saying (he cites Stein) "Our wish is that Arabian countries shall be for the Arabs, Armenia for the Armenians and Judaea for the Jews".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAuron2017278_219-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAuron2017278-219">[174]</a></sup>

The following October [Neville Chamberlain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neville_Chamberlain "Neville Chamberlain"), while chairing a Zionist meeting, discussed a "new Jewish State."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedman1973313_216-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedman1973313-216">[171]</a></sup> At the time, Chamberlain was a Member of Parliament for [Ladywood, Birmingham](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Birmingham_Ladywood_(UK_Parliament_constituency) "Birmingham Ladywood (UK Parliament constituency)"); recalling the event in 1939, just after Chamberlain had approved the 1939 White Paper, the Jewish Telegraph Agency noted that the Prime Minister had "experienced a pronounced change of mind in the 21 years intervening"<sup id="cite_ref-220"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-220">[175]</a></sup> A year later, on the Declaration's second anniversary, General [Jan Smuts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jan_Smuts "Jan Smuts") said that Britain "would redeem her pledge ... and a great Jewish state would ultimately rise."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedman1973313_216-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedman1973313-216">[171]</a></sup> In similar vein, Churchill a few months later stated:

> If, as may well happen, there should be created in our own lifetime by the banks of the Jordan a Jewish State under the protection of the British Crown which might comprise three or four millions of Jews, an event will have occurred in the history of the world which would from every point of view be beneficial.<sup id="cite_ref-221"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-221">[176]</a></sup>

At the 22 June 1921 meeting of the Imperial Cabinet, Churchill was asked by [Arthur Meighen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arthur_Meighen "Arthur Meighen"), the Canadian Prime Minister, about the meaning of the national home. Churchill said "If in the course of many years they become a majority in the country, they naturally would take it over ... pro rata with the Arab. We made an equal pledge that we would not turn the Arab off his land or invade his political and social rights".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJohnson2013441_222-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJohnson2013441-222">[177]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/The_Future_of_Palestine%2C_Lord_Curzon%27s_October_1917_cabinet_memorandum%2C_one_week_prior_to_the_Balfour_Declaration.jpg/220px-The_Future_of_Palestine%2C_Lord_Curzon%27s_October_1917_cabinet_memorandum%2C_one_week_prior_to_the_Balfour_Declaration.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:The_Future_of_Palestine,_Lord_Curzon%27s_October_1917_cabinet_memorandum,_one_week_prior_to_the_Balfour_Declaration.jpg)

Lord Curzon's 26 October 1917 cabinet memorandum, circulated one week prior to the declaration, addressed the meaning of the phrase "a National Home for the Jewish race in Palestine", noting the range of different opinions<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECurzon1917_211-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTECurzon1917-211">[167]</a></sup>

Responding to Curzon in January 1919, Balfour wrote "Weizmann has never put forward a claim for the Jewish Government of Palestine. Such a claim in my opinion is clearly inadmissible and personally I do not think we should go further than the original declaration which I made to Lord Rothschild".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELieshout2016387_223-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTELieshout2016387-223">[178]</a></sup>

In February 1919, France issued a statement that it would not oppose putting Palestine under British trusteeship and the formation of a Jewish State.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedman1973313_216-4"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedman1973313-216">[171]</a></sup> Friedman further notes that France's attitude went on to change;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedman1973313_216-5"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedman1973313-216">[171]</a></sup> Yehuda Blum, while discussing France's "unfriendly attitude towards the Jewish national movement", notes the content of a report made by Robert Vansittart (a leading member of the British delegation to the Paris Peace Conference) to Curzon in November 1920 which said:

> \[The French\] had agreed to a Jewish National Home, not a Jewish State. They considered we were steering straight upon the latter, and the very last thing they would do was to enlarge that State for they totally disapproved our policy.<sup id="cite_ref-224"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-224">[179]</a></sup>

Greece's Foreign Minister told the editor of the Salonica Jewish organ Pro-Israel that "the establishment of a Jewish State meets in Greece with full and sincere sympathy ... A Jewish Palestine would become an ally of Greece."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedman1973313_216-6"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedman1973313-216">[171]</a></sup> In [Switzerland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Switzerland "Switzerland"), a number of noted historians including professors Tobler, Forel-Yvorne, and Rogaz, supported the idea of establishing a Jewish state, with one referring to it as "a sacred right of the Jews."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedman1973313_216-7"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedman1973313-216">[171]</a></sup> While in [Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Germany "Germany"), officials and most of the press took the Declaration to mean a British sponsored state for the Jews.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedman1973313_216-8"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedman1973313-216">[171]</a></sup>

The British government, including Churchill, made it clear that the Declaration did not intend for the whole of Palestine to be converted into a Jewish National Home, "but that such a Home should be founded in Palestine."<sup id="cite_ref-228"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-228">[xxii]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-233"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-233">[xxiii]</a></sup> [Emir Faisal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Faisal_I_of_Iraq "Faisal I of Iraq"), King of Syria and Iraq, made a formal written agreement with Zionist leader [Chaim Weizmann](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chaim_Weizmann "Chaim Weizmann"), which was drafted by T.E. Lawrence, whereby they would try to establish a peaceful relationship between Arabs and Jews in Palestine.<sup id="cite_ref-Sekulow_234-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-Sekulow-234">[186]</a></sup> The 3 January 1919 [Faisal–Weizmann Agreement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Faisal%E2%80%93Weizmann_Agreement "Faisal–Weizmann Agreement") was a short-lived agreement for Arab–Jewish cooperation on the development of a Jewish homeland in Palestine.<sup id="cite_ref-236"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-236">[z]</a></sup> Faisal did treat Palestine differently in his presentation to the Peace Conference on 6 February 1919 saying "Palestine, for its universal character, \[should be\] left on one side for the mutual consideration of all parties concerned".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedman197392_237-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedman197392-237">[188]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-238"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-238">[189]</a></sup> The agreement was never implemented.<sup id="cite_ref-241"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-241">[aa]</a></sup> In a subsequent letter written in English by Lawrence for Faisal's signature, he explained:

> We feel that the Arabs and Jews are cousins in race, suffering similar oppression at the hands of powers stronger than themselves, and by a happy coincidence have been able to take the first step toward the attainment of their national ideals together. We Arabs, especially the educated among us, look with deepest sympathy on the Zionist movement ... We will do our best, in so far as we are concerned, to help them through; we will wish the Jews a most hearty welcome home.<sup id="cite_ref-Sekulow_234-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-Sekulow-234">[186]</a></sup>

When the letter was tabled at the [Shaw Commission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shaw_Commission "Shaw Commission") in 1929, [Rustam Haidar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rustam_Haidar "Rustam Haidar") spoke to Faisal in Baghdad and cabled that Faisal had "no recollection that he wrote anything of the sort".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllawi2014215_242-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllawi2014215-242">[192]</a></sup> In January 1930, Haidar wrote to a newspaper in Baghdad that Faisal: "finds it exceedingly strange that such a matter is attributed to him as he at no time would consider allowing any foreign nation to share in an Arab country".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllawi2014215_242-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllawi2014215-242">[192]</a></sup> [Awni Abd al-Hadi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Awni_Abd_al-Hadi "Awni Abd al-Hadi"), Faisal's secretary, wrote in his memoirs that he was not aware that a meeting between Frankfurter and Faisal took place and that: "I believe that this letter, assuming that it is authentic, was written by Lawrence, and that Lawrence signed it in English on behalf of Faisal. I believe this letter is part of the false claims made by Chaim Weizmann and Lawrence to lead astray public opinion."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllawi2014215_242-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllawi2014215-242">[192]</a></sup> According to Allawi, the most likely explanation for the Frankfurter letter is that a meeting took place, a letter was drafted in English by Lawrence, but that its "contents were not entirely made clear to Faisal. He then may or may not have been induced to sign it", since it ran counter to Faisal's other public and private statements at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllawi2014216–217_243-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllawi2014216%E2%80%93217-243">[193]</a></sup> A 1 March interview by Le Matin quoted Faisal as saying:

> This feeling of respect for other religions dictates my opinion about Palestine, our neighbor. That the unhappy Jews come to reside there and behave as good citizens of this country, our humanity rejoices given that they are placed under a Muslim or Christian government mandated by The League of Nations. If they want to constitute a state and claim sovereign rights in this region, I foresee very serious dangers. It is to be feared that there will be a conflict between them and the other races.<sup id="cite_ref-244"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-244">[194]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-245"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-245">[ab]</a></sup>

Referring to his 1922 [White Paper](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Churchill_White_Paper "Churchill White Paper"), Churchill later wrote that "there is nothing in it to prohibit the ultimate establishment of a Jewish State."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUNSCOP1947II,_Art._77_246-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUNSCOP1947II,_Art._77-246">[195]</a></sup> And in private, many British officials agreed with the Zionists' interpretation that a state would be established when a Jewish majority was achieved.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMansfield1992176–177_247-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMansfield1992176%E2%80%93177-247">[196]</a></sup>

When Chaim Weizmann met with Churchill, Lloyd George and Balfour at Balfour's home in London on 21 July 1921, Lloyd George and Balfour assured Weizmann "that by the Declaration they had always meant an eventual Jewish State," according to Weizmann minutes of that meeting.<sup id="cite_ref-248"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-248">[197]</a></sup> Lloyd George stated in 1937 that it was intended that Palestine would become a Jewish Commonwealth if and when Jews "had become a definite majority of the inhabitants",<sup id="cite_ref-250"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-250">[ac]</a></sup> and Leo Amery echoed the same position in 1946.<sup id="cite_ref-252"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-252">[ad]</a></sup> In the UNSCOP report of 1947, the issue of home versus state was subjected to scrutiny arriving at a similar conclusion to that of Lloyd George.<sup id="cite_ref-255"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-255">[xxiv]</a></sup>

### Scope of the national home "in Palestine"

The statement that such a homeland would be found "in Palestine" rather than "of Palestine" was also deliberate.<sup id="cite_ref-Gelvin82_256-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-Gelvin82-256">[xxv]</a></sup> The proposed draft of the declaration contained in Rothschild's 12 July letter to Balfour referred to the principle "that Palestine should be reconstituted as the National Home of the Jewish people."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStein1961470_257-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStein1961470-257">[202]</a></sup> In the final text, following Lord Milner's amendment, the word "reconstituted" was removed and the word "that" was replaced with "in".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedman1973257_258-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedman1973257-258">[203]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERenton201621_259-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTERenton201621-259">[204]</a></sup>

This text thereby avoided committing the entirety of Palestine as the National Home of the Jewish people, resulting in controversy in future years over the intended scope, especially the [Revisionist Zionism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Revisionist_Zionism "Revisionist Zionism") sector, which claimed entirety of [Mandatory Palestine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mandatory_Palestine "Mandatory Palestine") and [Emirate of Transjordan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emirate_of_Transjordan "Emirate of Transjordan") as [Jewish Homeland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_Homeland "Jewish Homeland")<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHalpern1987163_189-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHalpern1987163-189">[150]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedman1973257_258-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedman1973257-258">[203]</a></sup> This was clarified by the 1922 Churchill White Paper, which wrote that "the terms of the declaration referred to do not contemplate that Palestine as a whole should be converted into a Jewish National Home, but that such a Home should be founded 'in Palestine.'"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECaplan201174_260-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTECaplan201174-260">[205]</a></sup>

The declaration did not include any geographical boundaries for Palestine.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBiger200449_261-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBiger200449-261">[206]</a></sup> Following the end of the war, three documents – the declaration, the Hussein-McMahon Correspondence and the Sykes-Picot Agreement – became the basis for the negotiations to set the boundaries of Palestine.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBiger200451_262-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBiger200451-262">[207]</a></sup>

### Civil and religious rights of non-Jewish communities in Palestine

> "If, however, the strict terms of the Balfour Statement are adhered to ... it can hardly be doubted that the extreme Zionist Program must be greatly modified. For "a national home for the Jewish people" is not equivalent to making Palestine into a Jewish State; nor can the erection of such a Jewish State be accomplished without the gravest trespass upon the "civil and religious rights of existing non-Jewish communities in Palestine." The fact came out repeatedly in the Commission's conference with Jewish representatives, that the Zionists looked forward to a practically complete dispossession of the present non-Jewish inhabitants of Palestine, by various forms of purchase."

Report of the [King–Crane Commission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/King%E2%80%93Crane_Commission "King–Crane Commission"), August 1919<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBickertonKlausner2016109_263-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBickertonKlausner2016109-263">[208]</a></sup>

The declaration's first safeguard clause referred to protecting the [civil and religious rights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_rights "Human rights") of non-Jews in Palestine. The clause had been drafted together with the second safeguard by Leo Amery in consultation with Lord Milner, with the intention to "go a reasonable distance to meeting the objectors, both Jewish and pro-Arab, without impairing the substance of the proposed declaration".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELieshout2016221_264-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTELieshout2016221-264">[209]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-266"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-266">[ae]</a></sup>

The "non-Jews" constituted 90% of the population of Palestine;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalin_Commission192011_267-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalin_Commission192011-267">[211]</a></sup> in the words of [Ronald Storrs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ronald_Storrs "Ronald Storrs"), Britain's Military Governor of Jerusalem between 1917 and 1920, the community observed that they had been "not so much as named, either as Arabs, Moslems or Christians, but were lumped together under the negative and humiliating definition of 'Non-Jewish Communities' and relegated to subordinate provisos".<sup id="cite_ref-Storrs43_270-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-Storrs43-270">[af]</a></sup> The community also noted that there was no reference to protecting their "political status" or political rights, as there was in the subsequent safeguard relating to Jews in other countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStorrs194351_268-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStorrs194351-268">[212]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHardieHerrman198088_269-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHardieHerrman198088-269">[213]</a></sup> This protection was frequently contrasted against the commitment to the Jewish community, and over the years a variety of terms were used to refer to these two obligations as a pair;<sup id="cite_ref-Dual_274-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-Dual-274">[ag]</a></sup> a particularly heated question was whether these two obligations had "equal weight", and in 1930 this equal status was confirmed by the [Permanent Mandates Commission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Permanent_Mandates_Commission "Permanent Mandates Commission") and by the British government in the [Passfield white paper](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Passfield_white_paper "Passfield white paper").<sup id="cite_ref-276"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-276">[ah]</a></sup>

Balfour stated in February 1919 that Palestine was considered an exceptional case in which, referring to the local population, "we deliberately and rightly decline to accept the principle of [self-determination](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-determination "Self-determination"),"<sup id="cite_ref-278"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-278">[ai]</a></sup> although he considered that the policy provided self-determination to Jews.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBalfour192814,_25_279-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBalfour192814,_25-279">[219]</a></sup> Avi Shlaim considers this the declaration's "greatest contradiction".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShlaim2005251–270_116-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShlaim2005251%E2%80%93270-116">[90]</a></sup> This principle of self-determination had been declared on numerous occasions subsequent to the declaration – President Wilson's January 1918 [Fourteen Points](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fourteen_Points "Fourteen Points"), McMahon's Declaration to the Seven in June 1918, the November 1918 [Anglo-French Declaration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anglo-French_Declaration "Anglo-French Declaration"), and the June 1919 [Covenant of the League of Nations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Covenant_of_the_League_of_Nations "Covenant of the League of Nations") that had established the [mandate system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/League_of_Nations_mandate "League of Nations mandate").<sup id="cite_ref-283"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-283">[aj]</a></sup> In an August 1919 memo Balfour acknowledged the inconsistency among these statements, and further explained that the British had no intention of consulting the existing population of Palestine.<sup id="cite_ref-Balfour1919q_286-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-Balfour1919q-286">[ak]</a></sup> The results of the ongoing American [King–Crane Commission of Enquiry consultation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/King%E2%80%93Crane_Commission "King–Crane Commission") of the local population – from which the British had withdrawn – were suppressed for three years until the report was leaked in 1922.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGelvin199913–29_287-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGelvin199913%E2%80%9329-287">[225]</a></sup> Subsequent British governments have acknowledged this deficiency, in particular the 1939 committee led by the [Lord Chancellor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lord_Chancellor "Lord Chancellor"), [Frederic Maugham](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frederic_Maugham,_1st_Viscount_Maugham "Frederic Maugham, 1st Viscount Maugham"), which concluded that the government had not been "free to dispose of Palestine without regard for the wishes and interests of the inhabitants of Palestine",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKhouri19859_288-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKhouri19859-288">[226]</a></sup> and the April 2017 statement by British Foreign Office minister of state [Baroness Anelay](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joyce_Anelay,_Baroness_Anelay_of_St_Johns "Joyce Anelay, Baroness Anelay of St Johns") that the government acknowledged that "the Declaration should have called for the protection of political rights of the non-Jewish communities in Palestine, particularly their right to self-determination."<sup id="cite_ref-291"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-291">[al]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-293"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-293">[am]</a></sup>

### Rights and political status of Jews in other countries

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/The_Anti-Semitism_of_the_Present_Government%2C_Edwin_Montagu%2C_23_August_1917.jpg/220px-The_Anti-Semitism_of_the_Present_Government%2C_Edwin_Montagu%2C_23_August_1917.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:The_Anti-Semitism_of_the_Present_Government,_Edwin_Montagu,_23_August_1917.jpg)

[Edwin Montagu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edwin_Montagu "Edwin Montagu"), the only Jew in a senior British government position,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchneer2010193_294-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchneer2010193-294">[230]</a></sup> wrote a 23 August 1917 memorandum stating his belief that: "the policy of His Majesty's Government is anti-Semitic in result and will prove a rallying ground for anti-Semites in every country of the world."

The second safeguard clause was a commitment that nothing should be done which might prejudice the rights of the Jewish communities in other countries outside of Palestine.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchneer2010336_295-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchneer2010336-295">[231]</a></sup> The original drafts of Rothschild, Balfour, and Milner did not include this safeguard, which was drafted together with the preceding safeguard in early October,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchneer2010336_295-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchneer2010336-295">[231]</a></sup> in order to reflect opposition from influential members of the Anglo-Jewish community.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchneer2010336_295-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchneer2010336-295">[231]</a></sup> Lord Rothschild took exception to the proviso on the basis that it presupposed the possibility of a danger to non-Zionists, which he denied.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIngrams200913_296-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIngrams200913-296">[232]</a></sup>

The Conjoint Foreign Committee of the [Board of Deputies of British Jews](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Board_of_Deputies_of_British_Jews "Board of Deputies of British Jews") and the [Anglo-Jewish Association](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anglo-Jewish_Association "Anglo-Jewish Association") had published a letter in _[The Times](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Times "The Times")_ on 24 May 1917 entitled _Views of Anglo-Jewry_, signed by the two organisations' presidents, [David Lindo Alexander](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Lindo_Alexander "David Lindo Alexander") and [Claude Montefiore](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Claude_Montefiore "Claude Montefiore"), stating their view that: "the establishment of a Jewish nationality in Palestine, founded on this theory of homelessness, must have the effect throughout the world of stamping the Jews as strangers in their native lands, and of undermining their hard-won position as citizens and nationals of these lands."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELieshout2016214_297-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTELieshout2016214-297">[233]</a></sup> This was followed in late August by [Edwin Montagu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edwin_Montagu "Edwin Montagu"), an influential [anti-Zionist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Zionist "Anti-Zionist") Jew and [Secretary of State for India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_India "Secretary of State for India"), and the only Jewish member of the British Cabinet, who wrote in a Cabinet memorandum that: "The policy of His Majesty's Government is anti-Semitic in result and will prove a rallying ground for anti-Semites in every country of the world."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMakdisi2010239_298-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMakdisi2010239-298">[234]</a></sup>

## Reaction

The text of the declaration was published in the press one week after it was signed, on 9 November 1917.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchneer2010342_299-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchneer2010342-299">[235]</a></sup> Other related events took place within a short timeframe, the two most relevant being the almost immediate British military capture of Palestine and the leaking of the previously secret Sykes-Picot Agreement. On the military side, both [Gaza](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Third_Battle_of_Gaza "Third Battle of Gaza") and [Jaffa fell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Jaffa_(1917) "Battle of Jaffa (1917)") within several days, and [Jerusalem was surrendered](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Jerusalem "Battle of Jerusalem") to the British on 9 December.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGrainger2006109–114_123-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGrainger2006109%E2%80%93114-123">[97]</a></sup> The publication of the Sykes–Picot Agreement, following the Russian Revolution, in the Bolshevik _[Izvestia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Izvestia "Izvestia")_ and _[Pravda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pravda "Pravda")_ on 23 November 1917 and in the British _[Manchester Guardian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Guardian "The Guardian")_ on 26 November 1917, represented a dramatic moment for the Allies' Eastern campaign:<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUlrichsenUlrichsen2014157_300-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUlrichsenUlrichsen2014157-300">[236]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllawi2014108_301-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllawi2014108-301">[237]</a></sup> "the British were embarrassed, the Arabs dismayed and the Turks delighted."<sup id="cite_ref-302"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-302">[238]</a></sup> The Zionists had been aware of the outlines of the agreement since April and specifically the part relevant to Palestine, following a meeting between Weizmann and Cecil where Weizmann made very clear his objections to the proposed scheme.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchneer2010223_303-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchneer2010223-303">[239]</a></sup>

### Zionist reaction

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Balfour_Declaration_in_the_Times_9_November_1917.jpg/220px-Balfour_Declaration_in_the_Times_9_November_1917.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Balfour_Declaration_in_the_Times_9_November_1917.jpg)

Balfour Declaration as published in _[The Times](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Times "The Times")_, 9 November 1917

The declaration represented the first public support for Zionism by a major political power<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECaplan201178_304-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTECaplan201178-304">[240]</a></sup> – its publication galvanized Zionism, which finally had obtained an official charter.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStein2003129_305-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStein2003129-305">[241]</a></sup> In addition to its publication in major newspapers, leaflets were circulated throughout Jewish communities. These leaflets were [airdropped](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Airdrop "Airdrop") over Jewish communities in Germany and Austria, as well as the [Pale of Settlement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pale_of_Settlement "Pale of Settlement"), which [had been given to the Central Powers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Brest-Litovsk_(Ukraine%E2%80%93Central_Powers) "Treaty of Brest-Litovsk (Ukraine–Central Powers)") following the Russian withdrawal.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalestine_Royal_Commission193723_306-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalestine_Royal_Commission193723-306">[242]</a></sup>

Weizmann had argued that the declaration would have three effects: it would swing Russia to maintain pressure on Germany's [Eastern Front](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_I) "Eastern Front (World War I)"), since Jews had been prominent in the [March Revolution of 1917](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/February_Revolution "February Revolution"); it would rally the large Jewish community in the United States to press for greater funding for the [American war effort](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_entry_into_World_War_I "American entry into World War I"), underway since April of that year; and, lastly, that it would undermine German Jewish support for [Kaiser Wilhelm II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wilhelm_II,_German_Emperor "Wilhelm II, German Emperor").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWatts2008190a_307-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWatts2008190a-307">[243]</a></sup>

The declaration spurred an unintended and extraordinary increase in the number of adherents of American Zionism; in 1914 the 200 American Zionist societies comprised a total of 7,500 members, which grew to 30,000 members in 600 societies in 1918 and 149,000 members in 1919.<sup id="cite_ref-Reinharz2_308-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-Reinharz2-308">[xxvi]</a></sup> Whilst the British had considered that the declaration reflected a previously established dominance of the Zionist position in Jewish thought, it was the declaration itself that was subsequently responsible for Zionism's legitimacy and leadership.<sup id="cite_ref-310"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-310">[xxvii]</a></sup>

Exactly one month after the declaration was issued, a large-scale celebration took place at the [Royal Opera House](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Royal_Opera_House "Royal Opera House") – speeches were given by leading Zionists as well as members of the British administration including Sykes and Cecil.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESokolow191999–116_311-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTESokolow191999%E2%80%93116-311">[245]</a></sup> From 1918 until the [Second World War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_World_War "Second World War"), Jews in [Mandatory Palestine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mandatory_Palestine "Mandatory Palestine") celebrated [Balfour Day](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Day "Balfour Day") as an annual national holiday on 2 November.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESorek201525_312-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTESorek201525-312">[246]</a></sup> The celebrations included ceremonies in schools and other public institutions and festive articles in the Hebrew press.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESorek201525_312-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTESorek201525-312">[246]</a></sup> In August 1919 Balfour approved Weizmann's request to name the first post-war settlement in Mandatory Palestine, "[Balfouria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfouria "Balfouria")", in his honour.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETomes2002198_313-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTETomes2002198-313">[247]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGlass2002199_314-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGlass2002199-314">[248]</a></sup> It was intended to be a model settlement for future American Jewish activity in Palestine.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGlass2002200_315-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGlass2002200-315">[249]</a></sup>

Herbert Samuel, the Zionist MP whose 1915 memorandum had framed the start of discussions in the British Cabinet, was asked by Lloyd George on 24 April 1920 to act as the first [civil governor of British Palestine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/High_Commissioners_for_Palestine_and_Transjordan "High Commissioners for Palestine and Transjordan"), replacing the [previous military administration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Occupied_Enemy_Territory_Administration "Occupied Enemy Territory Administration") that had ruled the area since the war.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHuneidi200194_316-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuneidi200194-316">[250]</a></sup> Shortly after beginning the role in July 1920, he was invited to read the _[haftarah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haftarah "Haftarah")_ from [Isaiah 40](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isaiah_40 "Isaiah 40") at the [Hurva Synagogue](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hurva_Synagogue "Hurva Synagogue") in Jerusalem,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDomnitch2000111–112_317-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDomnitch2000111%E2%80%93112-317">[251]</a></sup> which, according to his memoirs, led the congregation of older settlers to feel that the "fulfilment of ancient prophecy might at last be at hand".<sup id="cite_ref-319"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-319">[an]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHuneidi200196_320-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuneidi200196-320">[253]</a></sup>

### Opposition in Palestine

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Filastin_%28La_Palestine%29_March_25th_1925_editorial_addressed_to_Lord_Balfour.pdf/page1-220px-Filastin_%28La_Palestine%29_March_25th_1925_editorial_addressed_to_Lord_Balfour.pdf.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Filastin_(La_Palestine)_March_25th_1925_editorial_addressed_to_Lord_Balfour.pdf)

The most popular Palestinian Arab newspaper, _[Filastin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Filastin_(newspaper) "Filastin (newspaper)")_, published a four-page editorial addressed to Lord Balfour in March 1925. The editorial begins with ["J'Accuse!", in a reference to the outrage at French anti-semitism 27 years previously](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/J%27Accuse%E2%80%A6! "J'Accuse…!").

The local Christian and Muslim community of Palestine, who constituted [almost 90% of the population](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Demographic_history_of_Palestine_(region) "Demographic history of Palestine (region)"), strongly opposed the declaration.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalin_Commission192011_267-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalin_Commission192011-267">[211]</a></sup> As described by the Palestinian-American philosopher [Edward Said](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edward_Said "Edward Said") in 1979, it was perceived as being made: "(a) by a European power, (b) about a non-European territory, (c) in a flat disregard of both the presence and the wishes of the native majority resident in that territory, and (d) it took the form of a promise about this same territory to another foreign group."<sup id="cite_ref-Said_322-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-Said-322">[xxviii]</a></sup>

According to the 1919 King–Crane Commission, "No British officer, consulted by the Commissioners, believed that the Zionist programme could be carried out except by force of arms."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedman2000273_323-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedman2000273-323">[255]</a></sup> A delegation of the [Muslim-Christian Association](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslim-Christian_Associations "Muslim-Christian Associations"), headed by [Musa al-Husayni](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Musa_al-Husayni "Musa al-Husayni"), expressed public disapproval on 3 November 1918, one day after the Zionist Commission parade marking the first anniversary of the Balfour Declaration.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWasserstein199131_324-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWasserstein199131-324">[256]</a></sup> They handed a petition signed by more than 100 notables to Ronald Storrs, the British military governor:

> We have noticed yesterday a large crowd of Jews carrying banners and over-running the streets shouting words which hurt the feeling and wound the soul. They pretend with open voice that Palestine, which is the Holy Land of our fathers and the graveyard of our ancestors, which has been inhabited by the Arabs for long ages, who loved it and died in defending it, is now a national home for them ... We Arabs, Muslim and Christian, have always sympathized profoundly with the persecuted Jews and their misfortunes in other countries ... but there is wide difference between such sympathy and the acceptance of such a nation ... ruling over us and disposing of our affairs.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWasserstein199132_325-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWasserstein199132-325">[257]</a></sup>

The group also protested the carrying of new "white and blue banners with two inverted triangles in the middle",<sup id="cite_ref-Hun32_326-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-Hun32-326">[258]</a></sup> drawing the attention of the British authorities to the serious consequences of any political implications in raising the banners.<sup id="cite_ref-Hun32_326-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-Hun32-326">[258]</a></sup> Later that month, on the first anniversary of the occupation of [Jaffa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jaffa "Jaffa") by the British, the Muslim-Christian Association sent a lengthy memorandum and petition to the military governor protesting once more any formation of a Jewish state.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHuneidi200132a_327-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuneidi200132a-327">[259]</a></sup> The majority of Britain's military leaders considered Balfour's declaration either a mistake, or one that presented grave risks.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcTague197876_328-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcTague197876-328">[260]</a></sup>

### Broader Arab response

In the broader Arab world, the declaration was seen as a betrayal of the British wartime understandings with the Arabs.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWatts2008190a_307-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWatts2008190a-307">[243]</a></sup> The Sharif of Mecca and other Arab leaders considered the declaration a violation of a previous commitment made in the McMahon–Hussein correspondence in exchange for launching the Arab Revolt.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShlaim2005251–270_116-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShlaim2005251%E2%80%93270-116">[90]</a></sup>

Following the publication of the declaration in an Egyptian newspaper, _[Al Muqattam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Muqattam "Al Muqattam")_,<sup id="cite_ref-aida_329-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-aida-329">[261]</a></sup> the British dispatched Commander [David George Hogarth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_George_Hogarth "David George Hogarth") to see Hussein in January 1918 bearing [the message](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hogarth_Message "Hogarth Message") that the "political and economic freedom" of the Palestinian population was not in question.<sup id="cite_ref-Khouri_101-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-Khouri-101">[80]</a></sup> Hogarth reported that Hussein "would not accept an independent Jewish State in Palestine, nor was I instructed to warn him that such a state was contemplated by Great Britain".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHuneidi200166_330-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuneidi200166-330">[262]</a></sup> Hussein had also learned of the Sykes–Picot Agreement when it was leaked by the new [Soviet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union "Soviet Union") government in December 1917, but was satisfied by [two disingenuous messages](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bassett_Letter "Bassett Letter") from Sir [Reginald Wingate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reginald_Wingate "Reginald Wingate"), who had replaced McMahon as High Commissioner of Egypt, assuring him that the British commitments to the Arabs were still valid and that the Sykes–Picot Agreement was not a formal treaty.<sup id="cite_ref-Khouri_101-4"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-Khouri-101">[80]</a></sup>

Continuing Arab disquiet over Allied intentions also led during 1918 to the British [Declaration to the Seven](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Declaration_to_the_Seven "Declaration to the Seven") and the Anglo-French Declaration, the latter promising "the complete and final liberation of the peoples who have for so long been oppressed by the Turks, and the setting up of national governments and administrations deriving their authority from the free exercise of the initiative and choice of the indigenous populations".<sup id="cite_ref-Khouri_101-5"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-Khouri-101">[80]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-331"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-331">[263]</a></sup>

In 1919, King Hussein refused to ratify the Treaty of Versailles. After February, 1920, the British ceased to pay subsidy to him.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEParis2003249_332-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEParis2003249-332">[264]</a></sup> In August 1920, five days after the signing of the Treaty of Sèvres, which formally recognized the Kingdom of Hejaz, Curzon asked Cairo to procure Hussein's signature to both treaties and agreed to make a payment of £30,000 conditional on signature.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMousa1978184–5_333-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMousa1978184%E2%80%935-333">[265]</a></sup> Hussein declined and in 1921, stated that he could not be expected to "affix his name to a document assigning Palestine to the Zionists and Syria to foreigners."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMousa1978185_334-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMousa1978185-334">[266]</a></sup> Following the 1921 Cairo Conference, Lawrence was sent to try and obtain the King's signature to a treaty as well as to Versailles and Sèvres, a £60,000 annual subsidy being proposed; this attempt also failed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEParis2003252_335-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEParis2003252-335">[267]</a></sup> During 1923, the British made one further attempt to settle outstanding issues with Hussein and once again, the attempt foundered, Hussein continued in his refusal to recognize the Balfour Declaration or any of the Mandates that he perceived as being his domain. In March 1924, having briefly considered the possibility of removing the offending article from the treaty, the government suspended any further negotiations;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHuneidi200171–2_336-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuneidi200171%E2%80%932-336">[268]</a></sup> within six months they withdrew their support in favour of their [central Arabian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sultanate_of_Nejd "Sultanate of Nejd") ally [Ibn Saud](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ibn_Saud "Ibn Saud"), who proceeded to [conquer Hussein's kingdom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_conquest_of_Hejaz "Saudi conquest of Hejaz").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHuneidi200172_337-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuneidi200172-337">[269]</a></sup>

### Allies and Associated Powers

The declaration was first endorsed by a foreign government on 27 December 1917, when [Serbian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbia "Kingdom of Serbia") Zionist leader and diplomat [David Albala](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Albala "David Albala") announced the support of Serbia's [government in exile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Government_in_exile "Government in exile") during a [mission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diplomatic_mission "Diplomatic mission") to the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELebel2007159,_212–213_338-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTELebel2007159,_212%E2%80%93213-338">[270]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-339"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-339">[271]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMitrović201671_340-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMitrovi%C4%87201671-340">[272]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERock2019112_341-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTERock2019112-341">[273]</a></sup> The French and Italian governments offered their endorsements, on 14 February and 9 May 1918, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalestine_Royal_Commission193722_342-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalestine_Royal_Commission193722-342">[274]</a></sup> At a [private meeting in London on 1 December 1918](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1918_Clemenceau%E2%80%93Lloyd_George_Agreement_(Middle_East) "1918 Clemenceau–Lloyd George Agreement (Middle East)"), Lloyd George and French Prime Minister [Georges Clemenceau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georges_Clemenceau "Georges Clemenceau") agreed to certain modifications to the Sykes-Picot Agreement, including British control of Palestine.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERose201017_343-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTERose201017-343">[275]</a></sup>

On 25 April 1920, the [San Remo conference](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/San_Remo_conference "San Remo conference") – an outgrowth of the Paris Peace Conference attended by the prime ministers of Britain, France and Italy, the [Japanese Ambassador to France](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Category:Ambassadors_of_Japan_to_France "Category:Ambassadors of Japan to France"), and the [United States Ambassador to Italy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Ambassador_to_Italy "United States Ambassador to Italy") – established the basic terms for three League of Nations mandates: a French mandate for Syria, and British mandates for Mesopotamia and Palestine.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuigley201027–29_344-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuigley201027%E2%80%9329-344">[276]</a></sup> With respect to Palestine, the resolution stated that the British were responsible for putting into effect the terms of the Balfour Declaration.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuigley201029_345-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuigley201029-345">[277]</a></sup> The French and the Italians made clear their dislike of the "Zionist cast of the Palestinian mandate" and objected especially to language that did not safeguard the "political" rights of non-Jews, accepting Curzon's claim that "in the British language all ordinary rights were included in "civil rights"".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPedersen201535_346-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPedersen201535-346">[278]</a></sup> At the request of France, it was agreed that an undertaking was to be inserted in the mandate's [procès-verbal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proc%C3%A8s-verbal "Procès-verbal") that this would not involve the surrender of the rights hitherto enjoyed by the non-Jewish communities in Palestine.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuigley201029_345-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuigley201029-345">[277]</a></sup> The Italian endorsement of the Declaration had included the condition "... on the understanding that there is no prejudice against the legal and political status of the already existing religious communities ..." (in Italian "... che non ne venga nessun pregiudizio allo stato giuridico e politico delle gia esistenti communita religiose ..."<sup id="cite_ref-347"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-347">[279]</a></sup> The boundaries of Palestine were left unspecified, to "be determined by the Principal Allied Powers."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuigley201029_345-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuigley201029-345">[277]</a></sup> Three months later, in July 1920, the French defeat of Faisal's [Arab Kingdom of Syria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Kingdom_of_Syria "Arab Kingdom of Syria") precipitated the British need to know "what is the 'Syria' for which the French received a mandate at San Remo?" and "does it include Transjordania?"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilson199044_348-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilson199044-348">[280]</a></sup> – it subsequently decided to pursue a policy of associating [Transjordan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emirate_of_Transjordan "Emirate of Transjordan") with the mandated area of Palestine without adding it to the area of the Jewish National Home.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilson199044,_46–48_349-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilson199044,_46%E2%80%9348-349">[281]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWasserstein2008105–106_350-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWasserstein2008105%E2%80%93106-350">[282]</a></sup>

In 1922, Congress officially endorsed America's support for the Balfour Declaration through the passage of the [Lodge–Fish Resolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lodge%E2%80%93Fish_Resolution "Lodge–Fish Resolution"),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELebow1968501_181-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTELebow1968501-181">[143]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-351"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-351">[283]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrecher1987_352-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrecher1987-352">[284]</a></sup> notwithstanding opposition from the State Department.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavidson200227–30_353-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavidson200227%E2%80%9330-353">[285]</a></sup> Professor [Lawrence Davidson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lawrence_Davidson "Lawrence Davidson"), of [West Chester University](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Chester_University "West Chester University"), whose research focuses on American relations with the Middle East, argues that President Wilson and Congress ignored democratic values in favour of "biblical romanticism" when they endorsed the declaration.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavidson20021_354-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavidson20021-354">[286]</a></sup> He points to an organized pro-Zionist lobby in the United States, which was active at a time when the country's small [Arab American](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Americans "Arab Americans") community had little political power.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavidson20021_354-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavidson20021-354">[286]</a></sup>

### Central Powers

The publication of the Balfour Declaration was met with tactical responses from the Central Powers;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedman1997340–343_355-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedman1997340%E2%80%93343-355">[287]</a></sup> however the participation of the Ottoman Empire in the alliance meant that Germany was unable to effectively counter the British pronouncement.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPolkehn197589_356-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPolkehn197589-356">[288]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-357"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-357">[ao]</a></sup>

Two weeks following the declaration, [Ottokar Czernin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottokar_Czernin "Ottokar Czernin"), the Austrian Foreign Minister, gave an interview to [Arthur Hantke](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arthur_Menachem_Hantke "Arthur Menachem Hantke"), President of the [Zionist Federation of Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zionist_Federation_of_Germany "Zionist Federation of Germany"), promising that his government would influence the Turks once the war was over.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECohen1946120_358-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTECohen1946120-358">[289]</a></sup> On 12 December, the Ottoman [Grand Vizier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_Vizier "Grand Vizier"), [Talaat Pasha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Talaat_Pasha "Talaat Pasha"), gave an interview to the German newspaper _[Vossische Zeitung](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vossische_Zeitung "Vossische Zeitung")_<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECohen1946120_358-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTECohen1946120-358">[289]</a></sup> that was published on 31 December and subsequently released in the German-Jewish periodical _[Jüdische Rundschau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/J%C3%BCdische_Rundschau "Jüdische Rundschau")_ on 4 January 1918,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedman1997379_359-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedman1997379-359">[290]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECohen1946120_358-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTECohen1946120-358">[289]</a></sup> in which he referred to the declaration as "une blague"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECohen1946120_358-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTECohen1946120-358">[289]</a></sup> (a deception) and promised that under Ottoman rule "all justifiable wishes of the Jews in Palestine would be able to find their fulfilment" subject to the absorptive capacity of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECohen1946120_358-4"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTECohen1946120-358">[289]</a></sup> This Turkish statement was endorsed by the [German Foreign Office](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_Foreign_Office "Federal Foreign Office") on 5 January 1918.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECohen1946120_358-5"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTECohen1946120-358">[289]</a></sup> On 8 January 1918, a German-Jewish Society, the Union of German Jewish Organizations for the Protection of the Rights of the Jews of the East (VJOD),<sup id="cite_ref-360"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-360">[ap]</a></sup> was formed to advocate for further progress for Jews in Palestine.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEToury196881–84_361-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEToury196881%E2%80%9384-361">[291]</a></sup>

Following the war, the [Treaty of Sèvres](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_S%C3%A8vres "Treaty of Sèvres") was signed by the Ottoman Empire on 10 August 1920.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHuneidi200118–19_362-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuneidi200118%E2%80%9319-362">[292]</a></sup> The treaty dissolved the Ottoman Empire, requiring Turkey to renounce sovereignty over much of the Middle East.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHuneidi200118–19_362-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuneidi200118%E2%80%9319-362">[292]</a></sup> Article 95 of the treaty incorporated the terms of the Balfour Declaration with respect to "the administration of Palestine, within such boundaries as may be determined by the Principal Allied Powers".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHuneidi200118–19_362-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuneidi200118%E2%80%9319-362">[292]</a></sup> Since incorporation of the declaration into the Treaty of Sèvres did not affect the legal status of either the declaration or the Mandate, there was also no effect when Sèvres was superseded by the [Treaty of Lausanne](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Lausanne_(1923) "Treaty of Lausanne (1923)"), which did not include any reference to the declaration.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDe_Waart1994113_363-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDe_Waart1994113-363">[293]</a></sup>

In 1922, German [anti-Semitic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Semitic "Anti-Semitic") theorist [Alfred Rosenberg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alfred_Rosenberg "Alfred Rosenberg") in his primary [contribution to Nazi theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Racial_policy_of_Nazi_Germany "Racial policy of Nazi Germany") on Zionism,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHelmreich198524_364-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHelmreich198524-364">[294]</a></sup> _Der Staatsfeindliche Zionismus_ ("Zionism, the Enemy of the State"), accused German Zionists of working for a German defeat and supporting Britain and the implementation of the Balfour Declaration, in a version of the [stab-in-the-back myth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stab-in-the-back_myth "Stab-in-the-back myth").<sup id="cite_ref-366"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-366">[xxix]</a></sup> [Adolf Hitler](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adolf_Hitler "Adolf Hitler") took a similar approach in some of his speeches from 1920 onwards.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENicosia200867_365-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTENicosia200867-365">[295]</a></sup>

### The Holy See
