With the advent of the declaration and the British entry into Jerusalem on 9 December, the Vatican reversed its earlier sympathetic attitude to Zionism and adopted an oppositional stance that was [to continue until the early 1990s](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_See%E2%80%93Israel_relations "Holy See–Israel relations").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECiani201113_367-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTECiani201113-367">[296]</a></sup>

### Evolution of British opinion

> "It is said that the effect of the Balfour Declaration was to leave the Moslems and Christians dumbfounded ... It is impossible to minimise the bitterness of the awakening. They considered that they were to be handed over to an oppression which they hated far more than the Turk's and were aghast at the thought of this domination ... Prominent people openly talk of betrayal and that England has sold the country and received the price ... Towards the Administration \[the Zionists\] adopted the attitude of "We want the Jewish State and we won't wait", and they did not hesitate to avail themselves of every means open to them in this country and abroad to force the hand of an Administration bound to respect the "Status Quo" and to commit it, and thereby future Administrations, to a policy not contemplated in the Balfour Declaration ... What more natural than that \[the Moslems and Christians\] should fail to realise the immense difficulties the Administration was and is labouring under and come to the conclusion that the openly published demands of the Jews were to be granted and the guarantees in the Declaration were to become but a dead letter?"

Report of the [Palin Commission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palin_Commission "Palin Commission"), August 1920<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalin_Commission192010_368-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalin_Commission192010-368">[297]</a></sup>

The British policy as stated in the declaration was to face numerous challenges to its implementation in the following years. The first of these was the indirect peace negotiations which took place between Britain and the Ottomans in December 1917 and January 1918 during a pause in the hostilities for the rainy season;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGrainger2006218_369-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGrainger2006218-369">[298]</a></sup> although these peace talks were unsuccessful, archival records suggest that key members of the War Cabinet may have been willing to permit leaving Palestine under nominal Turkish sovereignty as part of an overall deal.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchneer2010347–360_370-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchneer2010347%E2%80%93360-370">[299]</a></sup>

In October 1919, almost a year after the end of the war, [Lord Curzon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Curzon,_1st_Marquess_Curzon_of_Kedleston "George Curzon, 1st Marquess Curzon of Kedleston") succeeded Balfour as Foreign Secretary. Curzon had been a member of the 1917 Cabinet that had approved the declaration, and according to British historian [Sir David Gilmour](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sir_David_Gilmour,_4th_Baronet "Sir David Gilmour, 4th Baronet"), Curzon had been "the only senior figure in the British government at the time who foresaw that its policy would lead to decades of Arab–Jewish hostility".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGilmour199667_371-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilmour199667-371">[300]</a></sup> He therefore determined to pursue a policy in line with its "narrower and more prudent rather than the wider interpretation".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGilmour199666_372-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilmour199666-372">[301]</a></sup> Following [Bonar Law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bonar_Law "Bonar Law")'s appointment as Prime Minister in late 1922, Curzon wrote to Law that he regarded the declaration as "the worst" of Britain's Middle East commitments and "a striking contradiction of our publicly declared principles".<sup id="cite_ref-373"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-373">[302]</a></sup>

In August 1920 the report of the [Palin Commission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palin_Commission "Palin Commission"), the first in a long line of British [Commissions of Inquiry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Public_inquiry "Public inquiry") on the question of Palestine during the Mandate period,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHuneidi200135_374-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuneidi200135-374">[303]</a></sup> noted that "The Balfour Declaration ... is undoubtedly the starting point of the whole trouble". The conclusion of the report, which was not published, mentioned the Balfour Declaration three times, stating that "the causes of the alienation and exasperation of the feelings of the population of Palestine" included:

-   "inability to reconcile the Allies' declared policy of self-determination with the Balfour Declaration, giving rise to a sense of betrayal and intense anxiety for their future";<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKattan200984_375-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKattan200984-375">[304]</a></sup>
-   "misapprehension of the true meaning of the Balfour Declaration and forgetfulness of the guarantees determined therein, due to the loose rhetoric of politicians and the exaggerated statements and writings of interested persons, chiefly Zionists";<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKattan200984_375-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKattan200984-375">[304]</a></sup> and
-   "Zionist indiscretion and aggression since the Balfour Declaration aggravating such fears".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKattan200984_375-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKattan200984-375">[304]</a></sup>

British public and government opinion became increasingly unfavourable to state support for Zionism; even Sykes had begun to change his views in late 1918.<sup id="cite_ref-377"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-377">[aq]</a></sup> In February 1922 Churchill telegraphed Samuel, who had begun his role as High Commissioner for Palestine 18 months earlier, asking for cuts in expenditure and noting:

> In both Houses of Parliament there is growing movement of hostility, against Zionist policy in Palestine, which will be stimulated by recent [Northcliffe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alfred_Harmsworth,_1st_Viscount_Northcliffe "Alfred Harmsworth, 1st Viscount Northcliffe") articles.<sup id="cite_ref-379"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-379">[ar]</a></sup> I do not attach undue importance to this movement, but it is increasingly difficult to meet the argument that it is unfair to ask the British taxpayer, already overwhelmed with taxation, to bear the cost of imposing on Palestine an unpopular policy.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHuneidi200157_380-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuneidi200157-380">[307]</a></sup>

Following the issuance of the Churchill White Paper in June 1922, the House of Lords rejected a Palestine Mandate that incorporated the Balfour Declaration by 60 votes to 25, following a motion issued by [Lord Islington](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Dickson-Poynder,_1st_Baron_Islington "John Dickson-Poynder, 1st Baron Islington").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHuneidi200158_381-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuneidi200158-381">[308]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-382"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-382">[309]</a></sup> The vote proved to be only symbolic as it was subsequently overruled by a vote in the House of Commons following a tactical pivot and variety of promises made by Churchill.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHuneidi200158_381-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuneidi200158-381">[308]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-385"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-385">[xxx]</a></sup>

In February 1923, following the change in government, Cavendish, in a lengthy memorandum for the Cabinet, laid the foundation for a secret review of Palestine policy:

> It would be idle to pretend that the Zionist policy is other than an unpopular one. It has been bitterly attacked in Parliament and is still being fiercely assailed in certain sections of the press. The ostensible grounds of attack are threefold:(1) the alleged violation of the McMahon pledges; (2) the injustice of imposing upon a country a policy to which the great majority of its inhabitants are opposed; and (3) the financial burden upon the British taxpayer ...<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuigley2011269_386-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuigley2011269-386">[312]</a></sup>

His covering note asked for a statement of policy to be made as soon as possible and that the cabinet ought to focus on three questions: (1) whether or not pledges to the Arabs conflict with the Balfour declaration; (2) if not, whether the new government should continue the policy set down by the old government in the 1922 White Paper; and (3) if not, what alternative policy should be adopted.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHuneidi199833_194-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuneidi199833-194">[154]</a></sup>

[Stanley Baldwin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stanley_Baldwin "Stanley Baldwin"), replacing Bonar Law as Prime Minister, in June 1923 set up a cabinet sub-committee whose terms of reference were:

> examine Palestine policy afresh and to advise the full Cabinet whether Britain should remain in Palestine and whether if she remained, the pro-Zionist policy should be continued.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECohen20106_387-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTECohen20106-387">[313]</a></sup>

The Cabinet approved the report of this committee on 31 July 1923. Describing it as "nothing short of remarkable", Quigley noted that the government was admitting to itself that its support for Zionism had been prompted by considerations having nothing to do with the merits of Zionism or its consequences for Palestine.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuigley2011279_388-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuigley2011279-388">[314]</a></sup> As Huneidi noted, "wise or unwise, it is well nigh impossible for any government to extricate itself without a substantial sacrifice of consistency and self-respect, if not honour."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHuneidi199837_389-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuneidi199837-389">[315]</a></sup>

The wording of the declaration was thus incorporated into the [British Mandate for Palestine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mandate_for_Palestine "Mandate for Palestine"), a legal instrument that created Mandatory Palestine with an explicit purpose of putting the declaration into effect and was finally formalized in September 1923.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERenton201616_390-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTERenton201616-390">[316]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalestine_Royal_Commission193731_391-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalestine_Royal_Commission193731-391">[317]</a></sup> Unlike the declaration itself, the Mandate was legally binding on the British government.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERenton201616_390-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTERenton201616-390">[316]</a></sup> In June 1924, Britain made its report to the Permanent Mandates Commission for the period July 1920 to the end of 1923 containing nothing of the candor reflected in the internal documents; the documents relating to the 1923 reappraisal stayed secret until the early 1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuigley2011280–2_392-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuigley2011280%E2%80%932-392">[318]</a></sup>

## Historiography and motivations

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Palestine_and_the_Balfour_Declaration%2C_Cabinet_Paper%2C_January_1923.jpg/200px-Palestine_and_the_Balfour_Declaration%2C_Cabinet_Paper%2C_January_1923.jpg)](https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/File:Palestine_and_the_Balfour_Declaration,_Cabinet_Paper,_January_1923.jpg "commons:File:Palestine and the Balfour Declaration, Cabinet Paper, January 1923.jpg")

"Palestine and the Balfour Declaration", Cabinet Paper reviewing the background to the declaration, January 1923

Lloyd George and Balfour remained in government until [the collapse of the coalition in October 1922](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carlton_Club_meeting "Carlton Club meeting").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDefries201488–90_393-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDefries201488%E2%80%9390-393">[319]</a></sup> Under [the new Conservative government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conservative_Government_1922%E2%80%9324 "Conservative Government 1922–24"), attempts were made to identify the background to and motivations for the declaration.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHuneidi200161–64_394-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuneidi200161%E2%80%9364-394">[320]</a></sup> A private Cabinet memorandum was produced in January 1923, providing a summary of the then-known Foreign Office and War Cabinet records leading up to the declaration. An accompanying Foreign Office note asserted that the primary authors of the declaration were Balfour, Sykes, Weizmann, and Sokolow, with "perhaps Lord Rothschild as a figure in the background", and that "negotiations seem to have been mainly oral and by means of private notes and memoranda of which only the scantiest records seem to be available."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHuneidi200161–64_394-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuneidi200161%E2%80%9364-394">[320]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHuneidi2001256_395-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuneidi2001256-395">[321]</a></sup>

Following the 1936 [general strike](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_general_strike_(Mandatory_Palestine) "Arab general strike (Mandatory Palestine)") that was to degenerate into the [1936–1939 Arab revolt in Palestine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine "1936–1939 Arab revolt in Palestine"), the most significant outbreak of violence since the Mandate began, a British [Royal Commission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Royal_Commission "Royal Commission") – a high-profile public inquiry – was appointed to investigate the causes of the unrest.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECaplan201194_396-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTECaplan201194-396">[322]</a></sup> The Palestine Royal Commission, appointed with significantly broader [terms of reference](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Terms_of_reference "Terms of reference") than the previous British inquiries into Palestine,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECaplan201194_396-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTECaplan201194-396">[322]</a></sup> completed its 404-page report after six months of work in June 1937, publishing it a month later.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECaplan201194_396-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTECaplan201194-396">[322]</a></sup> The report began by describing the history of the problem, including a detailed summary of the origins of the Balfour Declaration. Much of this summary relied on Lloyd-George's personal testimony;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalestine_Royal_Commission193722–28_397-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalestine_Royal_Commission193722%E2%80%9328-397">[323]</a></sup> Balfour had died in 1930 and Sykes in 1919.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKattan2009388–394_398-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKattan2009388%E2%80%93394-398">[324]</a></sup> He told the commission that the declaration was made "due to propagandist reasons ... In particular Jewish sympathy would confirm the support of American Jewry, and would make it more difficult for Germany to reduce her military commitments and improve her economic position on the eastern front".<sup id="cite_ref-PeelLG_399-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-PeelLG-399">[as]</a></sup> Two years later, in his _Memoirs of the Peace Conference_,<sup id="cite_ref-401"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-401">[at]</a></sup> Lloyd George described a total of nine factors motivating his decision as Prime Minister to release the declaration,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGelvin201482''ff''_196-6"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGelvin201482''ff''-196">[156]</a></sup> including the additional reasons that a Jewish presence in Palestine would strengthen Britain's position on the [Suez Canal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Canal "Suez Canal") and reinforce the route to their imperial dominion in India.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGelvin201482''ff''_196-7"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGelvin201482''ff''-196">[156]</a></sup>

These geopolitical calculations were debated and discussed in the following years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGelvin201482''ff''_196-8"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGelvin201482''ff''-196">[156]</a></sup> Historians agree that the British believed that expressing support would appeal to Jews in Germany and the United States, given two of Woodrow Wilson's closest advisors were known to be avid Zionists;<sup id="cite_ref-403"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-403">[xxxi]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-405"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-405">[xxxii]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-406"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-406">[328]</a></sup> they also hoped to encourage support from the large Jewish population in Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIngrams200916_407-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIngrams200916-407">[329]</a></sup> In addition, the British intended to pre-empt the expected French pressure for an international administration in Palestine.<sup id="cite_ref-410"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-410">[xxxiii]</a></sup>

Some historians argue that the British government's decision reflected what [James Gelvin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_L._Gelvin "James L. Gelvin"), Professor of Middle Eastern History at [UCLA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_California,_Los_Angeles "University of California, Los Angeles"), calls 'patrician anti-Semitism' in the overestimation of Jewish power in both the United States and Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGelvin201482''ff''_196-9"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGelvin201482''ff''-196">[156]</a></sup> American Zionism was still in its infancy; in 1914 the Zionist Federation had a small budget of about $5,000 and only 12,000 members, despite an American Jewish population of three million<sup id="cite_ref-412"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-412">[xxxiv]</a></sup> but the Zionist organizations had recently succeeded, following a show of force within the American Jewish community, in arranging a Jewish congress to debate the Jewish problem as a whole.<sup id="cite_ref-414"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-414">[xxxv]</a></sup> This impacted British and French government estimates of the balance of power within the American Jewish public.<sup id="cite_ref-Reinharz2_308-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-Reinharz2-308">[xxvi]</a></sup>

[Avi Shlaim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avi_Shlaim "Avi Shlaim"), Emeritus Professor of International Relations in the [University of Oxford](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Oxford "University of Oxford"), asserts that two main schools of thought have been developed on the question of the primary driving force behind the declaration,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShlaim2005251–270_116-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShlaim2005251%E2%80%93270-116">[90]</a></sup> one presented in 1961 by Leonard Stein,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStein1961_415-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStein1961-415">[334]</a></sup> a lawyer and former political secretary to the [World Zionist Organization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Zionist_Organization "World Zionist Organization"), and the other in 1970 by Mayir Vereté, then Professor of Israeli History at the [Hebrew University of Jerusalem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hebrew_University_of_Jerusalem "Hebrew University of Jerusalem").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVereté1970_416-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVeret%C3%A91970-416">[335]</a></sup> Shlaim states that Stein does not reach any clear cut conclusions, but that implicit in his narrative is that the declaration resulted primarily from the activity and skill of the Zionists, whereas according to Vereté, it was the work of hard-headed pragmatists motivated by British imperial interests in the Middle East.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShlaim2005251–270_116-4"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShlaim2005251%E2%80%93270-116">[90]</a></sup> Much of modern scholarship on the decision to issue the declaration focuses on the Zionist movement and rivalries within it,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith201150–51_417-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith201150%E2%80%9351-417">[336]</a></sup> with a key debate being whether the role of Weizmann was decisive or whether the British were likely to have issued a similar declaration in any event.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith201150–51_417-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith201150%E2%80%9351-417">[336]</a></sup> Danny Gutwein, Professor of Jewish History at the [University of Haifa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Haifa "University of Haifa"), proposes a twist on an old idea, asserting that Sykes's February 1917 approach to the Zionists was the defining moment, and that it was consistent with the pursuit of the government's wider agenda to [partition the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Partition_of_the_Ottoman_Empire "Partition of the Ottoman Empire").<sup id="cite_ref-418"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-418">[xxxvi]</a></sup> Historian [J. C. Hurewitz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/J._C._Hurewitz "J. C. Hurewitz") has written that British support for a Jewish homeland in Palestine was part of an effort to secure a land bridge between Egypt and the Persian Gulf by annexing territory from the Ottoman Empire.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHurewitz1979_419-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHurewitz1979-419">[337]</a></sup><sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (September 2020)">page&nbsp;needed</span></a></i>]</sup>

## Long-term impact

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Falastin_newspaper_front_page_2_November_1932_on_the_anniversary_of_the_Balfour_Declaration_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Falastin_newspaper_front_page_2_November_1932_on_the_anniversary_of_the_Balfour_Declaration_%28cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Falastin_newspaper_front_page_2_November_1932_on_the_anniversary_of_the_Balfour_Declaration_(cropped).jpg)

Falastin newspaper edition in 1932 featuring a caricature lamenting Balfour declaration's impacts on Palestine, showing Jewish immigration, and dispossession of Arab peasants

The declaration had two indirect consequences, the emergence of Israel and a chronic state of conflict between Arabs and Jews throughout the Middle East.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnited_Nations_Division_for_Palestinian_Rights1978_420-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnited_Nations_Division_for_Palestinian_Rights1978-420">[338]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWatts2008190_421-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWatts2008190-421">[339]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIngrams2009IX,_5_422-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIngrams2009IX,_5-422">[340]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchneer2010370,_376_423-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchneer2010370,_376-423">[341]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShlaim2005268_424-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShlaim2005268-424">[342]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETucker2017469–482_425-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTETucker2017469%E2%80%93482-425">[343]</a></sup> It has been described as the "[original sin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Original_sin "Original sin")" with respect to both Britain's failure in Palestine<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShlaim200923_426-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShlaim200923-426">[344]</a></sup> and for wider events in Palestine.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECohenKolinsky201388_427-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTECohenKolinsky201388-427">[345]</a></sup> The statement also had a significant impact on the traditional anti-Zionism of religious Jews, some of whom saw it as [divine providence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Divine_providence "Divine providence"); this contributed to the growth of [religious Zionism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religious_Zionism "Religious Zionism") amid the larger Zionist movement.<sup id="cite_ref-429"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-429">[xxxvii]</a></sup>

Starting in 1920, [intercommunal conflict in Mandatory Palestine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intercommunal_conflict_in_Mandatory_Palestine "Intercommunal conflict in Mandatory Palestine") broke out, which widened into the regional [Arab–Israeli conflict](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_conflict "Arab–Israeli conflict"), often referred to as the world's "most intractable conflict".<sup id="cite_ref-430"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-430">[347]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-431"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-431">[348]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-432"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-432">[349]</a></sup> The "dual obligation" to the two communities quickly proved to be untenable;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERenton2007151_433-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTERenton2007151-433">[350]</a></sup> the British subsequently concluded that it was impossible for them to pacify the two communities in Palestine by using different messages for different audiences.<sup id="cite_ref-435"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-435">[au]</a></sup> The Palestine Royal Commission – in making the first official proposal for partition of the region – referred to the requirements as "contradictory obligations",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalestine_Royal_Commission1937363_436-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalestine_Royal_Commission1937363-436">[352]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClevelandBunton2016244_437-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClevelandBunton2016244-437">[353]</a></sup> and that the "disease is so deep-rooted that, in our firm conviction, the only hope of a cure lies in a surgical operation".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalestine_Royal_Commission1937368_438-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalestine_Royal_Commission1937368-438">[354]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERose197382_439-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTERose197382-439">[355]</a></sup> Following the 1936–1939 Arab revolt in Palestine, and as worldwide tensions rose in the buildup to the Second World War, the British Parliament approved the [White Paper of 1939](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_Paper_of_1939 "White Paper of 1939") – their last formal statement of governing policy in Mandatory Palestine – declaring that Palestine should not become a Jewish State and placing restrictions on Jewish immigration.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewis2009175_440-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewis2009175-440">[356]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBerman199266_441-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBerman199266-441">[357]</a></sup> Whilst the British considered this consistent with the Balfour Declaration's commitment to protect the rights of non-Jews, many Zionists saw it as a repudiation of the declaration.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewis2009175_440-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewis2009175-440">[356]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBerman199266_441-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBerman199266-441">[357]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-444"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-444">[av]</a></sup> Although this policy lasted until the British surrendered the Mandate in 1948, it served only to highlight the fundamental difficulty for Britain in carrying out the Mandate obligations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUNSCOP1947_445-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUNSCOP1947-445">[360]</a></sup>

Britain's involvement in this became one of the most controversial parts of its Empire's history and damaged its reputation in the Middle East for generations.<sup id="cite_ref-Rose2_446-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-Rose2-446">[xxxviii]</a></sup> According to historian [Elizabeth Monroe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elizabeth_Monroe_(historian) "Elizabeth Monroe (historian)"): "measured by British interests alone, \[the declaration was\] one of the greatest mistakes in \[its\] imperial history."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMonroe198143_447-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMonroe198143-447">[361]</a></sup> The 2010 study by [Jonathan Schneer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jonathan_Schneer "Jonathan Schneer"), specialist in modern British history at [Georgia Tech](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georgia_Institute_of_Technology "Georgia Institute of Technology"), concluded that because the build-up to the declaration was characterized by "contradictions, deceptions, misinterpretations, and wishful thinking", the declaration sowed [dragon's teeth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dragon%27s_teeth_(mythology) "Dragon's teeth (mythology)") and "produced a murderous harvest, and we go on harvesting even today".<sup id="cite_ref-448"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-448">[xxxix]</a></sup> The foundational stone for modern Israel had been laid, but the prediction that this would lay the groundwork for harmonious Arab-Jewish cooperation proved to be wishful thinking.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchneer2010361_449-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchneer2010361-449">[362]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-451"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-451">[xl]</a></sup>

On the bicentenary of its foundation, the British newspaper _[The Guardian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Guardian "The Guardian")_, reflecting on its major errors of judgment, included the support the paper's editor, [C. P. Scott](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/C._P._Scott "C. P. Scott"), gave to Balfour's declaration. Israel had not become, it said, 'the country the Guardian foresaw or would have wanted.'<sup id="cite_ref-452"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-452">[364]</a></sup> The [Board of Deputies of British Jews](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Board_of_Deputies_of_British_Jews "Board of Deputies of British Jews") through its president [Marie van der Zyl](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marie_van_der_Zyl "Marie van der Zyl") denounced the column as 'breathtakingly ill-considered', declaring that the Guardian appeared "to do everything it can to undermine the legitimacy of the world's only Jewish state".<sup id="cite_ref-453"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-453">[365]</a></sup>

## The document

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/%D7%A9%D7%95%D7%9C%D7%97%D7%A0%D7%95_%D7%A9%D7%9C_%D7%91%D7%9C%D7%A4%D7%95%D7%A8.jpg/220px-%D7%A9%D7%95%D7%9C%D7%97%D7%A0%D7%95_%D7%A9%D7%9C_%D7%91%D7%9C%D7%A4%D7%95%D7%A8.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:%D7%A9%D7%95%D7%9C%D7%97%D7%A0%D7%95_%D7%A9%D7%9C_%D7%91%D7%9C%D7%A4%D7%95%D7%A8.jpg)

Lord Balfour's desk, in the [Museum of the Jewish Diaspora](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beth_Hatefutsoth "Beth Hatefutsoth") in Tel Aviv

The document was presented to the [British Museum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Museum "British Museum") in 1924 by [Walter Rothschild](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Walter_Rothschild "Walter Rothschild"); today it is held in the [British Library](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Library "British Library"), which separated from the British Museum in 1973, as Additional Manuscripts number 41178.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedman1973396,_note_65_454-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedman1973396,_note_65-454">[366]</a></sup> From October 1987 to May 1988 it was lent outside the UK for display in Israel's [Knesset](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knesset "Knesset").<sup id="cite_ref-TOI2016_455-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-TOI2016-455">[367]</a></sup>

-   [Proposals for a Jewish state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proposals_for_a_Jewish_state "Proposals for a Jewish state")

## Notes

### Primary supporting quotes

1.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-11 "Jump up")** Montefiore was the wealthiest British Jew, and leader of the [Board of Deputies of British Jews](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Board_of_Deputies_of_British_Jews "Board of Deputies of British Jews"). Charles Henry Churchill's first letter, in 1841, intended to catalyse an interest in Jewish emigration to Palestine: "Supposing that you and your colleagues should at once and earnestly interest yourselves upon this important subject of the recovery of your ancient country, it appears to me (forming my opinions upon the present attitude of affairs in the Turkish Empire) that it could only be as subjects of the Porte that you could commence to regain a footing in Palestine."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedman1973xxxii_10-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedman1973xxxii-10">[8]</a></sup>
2.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-38 "Jump up")** According to Weizmann's memoir, the conversation went as follows: "Mr. Balfour, supposing I was to offer you Paris instead of London, would you take it?" He sat up, looked at me, and answered: "But Dr. Weizmann, we have London." "That is true," I said, "but we had Jerusalem when London was a marsh." He ... said two things which I remember vividly. The first was: "Are there many Jews who think like you?" I answered: "I believe I speak the mind of millions of Jews whom you will never see and who cannot speak for themselves." ... To this he said: "If that is so you will one day be a force." Shortly before I withdrew, Balfour said: "It is curious. The Jews I meet are quite different." I answered: "Mr. Balfour, you meet the wrong kind of Jews".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeizmann1949111_37-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeizmann1949111-37">[28]</a></sup>
3.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-42 "Jump up")** Weizmann's notes of the meeting described that: "\[James\] thought that the Palestinian aspirations of the Jews will find a very favourable response in Government circles, which would support a project like that, both from a humanitarian and an English political point of view. The formation of a strong Jewish community in Palestine would be considered as a valuable political asset. He therefore thought that the demands which only amount to asking for an encouragement of colonization of Jews in Palestine are too modest and would not appeal sufficiently strongly to Statesmen. One should ask for something which is more than that and which tends towards the formation of a Jewish State."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGutwein2016120–130_41-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGutwein2016120%E2%80%93130-41">[31]</a></sup> Gutwein interpreted this discussion as follows: "James's recommendation that the Zionists should not stop at the demand for settlement of Jews in Palestine, but radicalize their demands for a Jewish state, reflected the political contrast between the reformists, who were prepared to support settlement of Jews in Palestine as part of the reorganization of the Ottoman Empire, and the radicals, who viewed a Jewish state as a means of partitioning it. Although James contended that the demand for a Jewish state would help in gaining the British statesmen's support, in view of Asquith's and Grey's opposition to this demand, it seems that the inaccuracy if not the misleading tenor of James's advice was meant to enlist Weizmann, and through him the Zionist movement, to assist the radicals and Lloyd George."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGutwein2016120–130_41-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGutwein2016120%E2%80%93130-41">[31]</a></sup>
4.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-Weiz1_67-0 "Jump up")** From Weizmann's memoirs: "The entry of Turkey into the fray and the remarks made by the Premier in his Guildhall speech were an additional impulse towards proceeding with the reconnoitring work at a higher speed ... An opportunity offered itself to discuss the Jewish problems with Mr. C. P. Scott (Editor of the Manchester Guardian)… Mr. Scott, who has, I believe, given the whole problem a very careful and sympathetic attention, was good enough to promise that he would talk to Mr. Lloyd George on the subject ... As it happened, Mr. Lloyd George, having several engagements for the week suggested that I should see Mr. Herbert Samuel, and an interview took place at his office. \[Footnote: 10 Dec. 1914\]"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeizmann1983122_66-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeizmann1983122-66">[53]</a></sup>
5.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-70 "Jump up")** Weizmann's memoirs: "He believed that my demands were too modest, that big things would have to be done in Palestine; he himself would move and would expect Jewry to move immediately the military situation was cleared up ... The Jews would have to bring sacrifices and he was prepared to do so. At this point I ventured to ask in which way the plans of Mr. Samuel were more ambitious than mine. Mr. Samuel preferred not to enter into a discussion of his plans, as he would like to keep them 'liquid', but he suggested that the Jews would have to build railways, harbours, a university, a network of schools, etc. ... He also thinks that perhaps the Temple may be rebuilt, as a symbol of Jewish unity, of course, in a modernised form."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeizmann1983122b_69-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeizmann1983122b-69">[55]</a></sup>
6.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-72 "Jump up")** Again from Weizmann's memoirs: "On the suggestion of Baron James, I went to see Sir Philip Magnus with whom I had a lengthy conversation, and he expressed his willingness to cooperate, provided that great discretion was used ... I asked Sir Philip his opinion of the advisability of seeing Mr. Balfour, and he thought that an interview with Mr. Balfour would be of very great interest and value ... At one of my visits to London I wrote to Mr. Balfour and got an appointment with him on Saturday the same week at 12 o'clock in his house.\[Footnote: 12 Dec. 1914\] I spoke to him practically in the same strain as I did to Mr. Samuel, but the whole turn of our conversation was more academic than practical."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeizmann1983126_71-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeizmann1983126-71">[56]</a></sup>
7.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-81 "Jump up")** Weizmann had been asked to produce a [new process for the production of acetone](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Acetone%E2%80%93butanol%E2%80%93ethanol_fermentation "Acetone–butanol–ethanol fermentation") in order to reduce the cost of [cordite](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cordite "Cordite") production;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewis2009115–119_65-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewis2009115%E2%80%93119-65">[52]</a></sup> the popular suggestion that this role influenced the decision to release the declaration has been described as "fanciful",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDefries201450_77-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDefries201450-77">[61]</a></sup> a "legend", a "myth",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECohen201447_78-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTECohen201447-78">[62]</a></sup> and "a product of \[Lloyd George's\] imagination".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewis2009115_79-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewis2009115-79">[63]</a></sup> From Lloyd George's _War Memoirs_, which created this myth: "But by the spring of 1915 the position in the American acetone market had become extremely delicate ... In the survey we made of all the various prospective requirements, it soon became clear that the supplies of wood alcohol for the manufacture of acetone would prove quite insufficient to meet the increasing demands, particularly in 1916 ... While I was casting about for some solution of the difficulty, I ran against the late C. P. Scott, Editor of the Manchester Guardian ... I took his word about Professor Weizmann and invited him to London to see me ... He could produce acetone by a fermentation process on a laboratory scale, but it would require some time before he could guarantee successful production on a manufacturing scale. In a few weeks' time he came to me and said: "The problem is solved."... When our difficulties were solved through Dr. Weizmann's genius I said to him: 'You have rendered great service to the State, and I should like to ask the Prime Minister to recommend you to His Majesty for some honour.' He said: 'There is nothing I want for myself.' 'But is there nothing we can do as a recognition of your valuable assistance to the country?' I asked.  He replied: 'Yes, I would like you to do something for my people.' He then explained his aspirations as to the repatriation of the Jews to the sacred land they had made famous. That was the fount and origin of the famous declaration about the National Home for Jews in Palestine. As soon as I became Prime Minister I talked the whole matter over with Mr. Balfour, who was then Foreign Secretary. As a scientist he was immensely interested when I told him of Dr. Weizmann's achievement. We were anxious at that time to gather Jewish support in neutral countries, notably in America. Dr. Weizmann was brought into direct contact with the Foreign Secretary. This was the beginning of an association, the outcome of which, after long examination, was the famous Balfour Declaration ..."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELloyd_George193350_80-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTELloyd_George193350-80">[64]</a></sup>
8.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-88 "Jump up")** See [the original 25 October 1915 letter here](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:McMahon%E2%80%93Hussein_Letter_25_October_1915.jpg "File:McMahon–Hussein Letter 25 October 1915.jpg"). [George Antonius](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Antonius "George Antonius") – who had been the first to publish the correspondence in full – described this letter as "by far the most important in the whole correspondence, and may perhaps be regarded as the most important international document in the history of the Arab national movement ... is still invoked as the main piece of evidence on which the Arabs accuse Great Britain of having broken faith with them."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAntonius1938169_87-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAntonius1938169-87">[69]</a></sup>
9.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-92 "Jump up")** In a 27 February 1916 letter, prior to his departure to Russia, Sykes wrote to Samuel: "I read [\[your 1915\] memorandum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Future_of_Palestine "The Future of Palestine") and have committed it to memory."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKamel2015109_90-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKamel2015109-90">[71]</a></sup> With respect to the borders, Sykes explained: "By excluding Hebron and the East of the Jordan there is less to discuss with the Moslems, as the Mosque of Omar then becomes the only matter of vital importance to discuss with them and further does away with any contact with the bedouins, who never cross the river except on business. I imagine that the principal object of Zionism is the realization of the ideal of an existing centre of nationality rather than boundaries or extent of territory."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESanders1984347_91-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTESanders1984347-91">[72]</a></sup>
10.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-96 "Jump up")** In his August 1919 memo Balfour noted, "In 1915 it was the Sherif of Mecca to whom the task of delimitation was to have been confided, nor were any restrictions placed upon his discretion in this matter, except certain reservations intended to protect French interests in Western Syria and Cilicia. In 1916 all this seems to have been forgotten. The Sykes–Picot Agreement made no reference to the Sherif of Mecca, and, so far as our five documents are concerned, he has never been heard of since. A wholly new method was adopted by France and England, who made with each other in the Sykes–Picot Agreement the rough and ready territorial arrangements already described—arrangements which the Allied and Associated Powers have so far neither explicitly accepted nor explicitly replaced."<sup id="cite_ref-Balfour1919_95-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-Balfour1919-95">[75]</a></sup>
11.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-104 "Jump up")** Sykes had discussed the matter with Picot, suggesting the creation of an Arab Sultanate of Palestine under French and British protection; he was reprimanded by Grey, Buchanan should tell Sykes 'to obliterate from his memory that Mr Samuel's Cabinet memorandum made any mention of a British protectorate and that I told Mr Samuel at the time that a British protectorate was quite out of the question and Sir M. Sykes should never mention the subject without making this clear'.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELieshout2016196_103-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTELieshout2016196-103">[82]</a></sup>
12.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-108 "Jump up")** The full text of the telegram to Sazonov may be found in Jeffries<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJeffries1939112–114_107-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJeffries1939112%E2%80%93114-107">[85]</a></sup>
13.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-109 "Jump up")** In ascertaining what Zionists will accept and what refuse I am guided by your telegram coupled with my memory of Mr Samuel's memorandum to the Cabinet in March 1915. Telegram say international regime unacceptable memorandum says French dominion equally unacceptable. As against this \[? French omitted\] \[If Picot represents them correctly\] would never consent to England having temporary or provisional charge of Palestine; not even if we offered Cyprus as a gift and appointed French Governor for Jerusalem Bethlehem Nazareth and Jaffa. They seem hardly normal on this subject and any reference seems to excite memories of all grievances from Joan of Arc to Fashoda
14.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-110 "Jump up")** Sykes was reprimanded by Grey, Buchanan should tell Sykes 'to obliterate from his memory that Mr Samuel's Cabinet memorandum made any mention of a British protectorate and that I told Mr Samuel at the time that a British protectorate was quite out of the question and Sir M. Sykes should never mention the subject without making this clear'.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELieshout2016196_103-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTELieshout2016196-103">[82]</a></sup>
15.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-128 "Jump up")** [Nahum Sokolow](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nahum_Sokolow "Nahum Sokolow") described the meeting in 1919 as follows: "The 7th of February 1917, constitutes a turning-point in the history ... At the commencement of the year 1917 Sir Mark Sykes entered into closer relations with Dr. Weizmann and the author, and the discussions held with the latter led to the meeting of February 7th, 1917, which marks the commencement of official negotiations. Besides Sir Mark Sykes, the following took part in this meeting: Lord Rothschild, Mr. Herbert Bentwich, Mr. Joseph Cowen, Dr. M. Gaster (at whose house the meeting took place), Mr. James de Rothschild, Mr. Harry Sacher, Right Hon. Herbert Samuel, M.P., Dr. Chaim Weizmann, and the author. The deliberations yielded a favourable result, and it was resolved to continue the work."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESokolow191952_127-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTESokolow191952-127">[99]</a></sup>
16.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-132 "Jump up")** Sykes had also informed the Zionists he was meeting Picot the following day and Sokolow was nominated by Rothschild to join the meeting which duly took place at Sykes' house. Sokolow was able to present the Zionists case and express his desire for a British protectorate although Picot declined to be drawn on this point. The day after that, Sokolow and Picot met alone at the French embassy, on this occasion Picot said "He personally would see that the facts about Zionism were communicated to the proper quarters and he would do his best to win for the movement whatever sympathies were necessary to be won so far as compatible with the French standpoint on this question."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchneer2010200_131-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchneer2010200-131">[102]</a></sup>
17.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-144 "Jump up")** The War Cabinet, reviewing this conference on 25 April, "inclined to the view that sooner or later the Sykes-Picot Agreement might have to be reconsidered ... No action should be taken at present in this matter".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELieshout2016281_142-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTELieshout2016281-142">[112]</a></sup>
18.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-148 "Jump up")** Sykes as _Chief Political Officer to the Egyptian Expeditionary Force_ and Picot as the _Haut-Commissaire Français pour Les Territoires Occupés en Palestine et en Syrie_ (High Commissioner for the Territories \[to be\] Occupied in Palestine and Syria), received their instructions on 3 April and 2 April respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELaurens1999305_146-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTELaurens1999305-146">[115]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELieshout2016203_147-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTELieshout2016203-147">[116]</a></sup> Sykes and Picot arrived in the Middle East at the end of April, and were to continue discussions until the end of May.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchneer2010227–236_145-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchneer2010227%E2%80%93236-145">[114]</a></sup>
19.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-161 "Jump up")** The Committee of the Jewish Communities (in Italian: _Comitato delle università israelitiche_) is known today as the Union of Italian Jewish Communities (in Italian: _Unione delle comunità ebraiche italiane_, abbreviated UCEI)
20.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-167 "Jump up")** In 1929, Zionist leader [Jacob de Haas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jacob_de_Haas "Jacob de Haas") wrote: "In May 1917 prior to the arrival of the Balfour Mission to the United States, President Wilson took occasion to afford ample opportunity for the discussion of Zionist Palestinian prospects, and the occasion was not neglected. At the first official reception given by President Wilson for Mr. Balfour, the latter singled out Brandeis as one with whom he desired private conversation. Mr. Balfour while in Washington summarized his own attitude in a single sentence, "I am a Zionist." But while Balfour and Brandeis met as often as circumstances demanded other Zionists met and discussed the Palestinian problem with all those members of the British mission whose understanding it was thought desirable to cultivate. This was made necessary because at that particular juncture the creation of an American mandatory for Palestine a policy Brandeis did not favour was being persistently discussed in the European press."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEde_Haas192989–90_166-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEde_Haas192989%E2%80%9390-166">[131]</a></sup>
21.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-169 "Jump up")** Ronald Graham wrote to [Lord Hardinge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_Hardinge,_1st_Baron_Hardinge_of_Penshurst "Charles Hardinge, 1st Baron Hardinge of Penshurst"), the [Permanent Under-Secretary of State for Foreign Affairs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Permanent_Under-Secretary_of_State_for_Foreign_Affairs "Permanent Under-Secretary of State for Foreign Affairs") (i.e. the most senior [civil servant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civil_Service_(United_Kingdom) "Civil Service (United Kingdom)"), or non-[minister](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minister_(government) "Minister (government)"), at the Foreign Office) on 13 June 1917: "It would appear that in view of the sympathy towards the Zionist movement which has already been expressed by the Prime Minister, Mr. Balfour, Lord R. Cecil, and other statesmen, we are committed to support it, although until Zionist policy has been more clearly defined our support must be of a general character. We ought, therefore, to secure all the political advantage we can out of our connection with Zionism, and there is no doubt that this advantage will be considerable, especially in Russia, where the only means of reaching the Jewish proletariat is through Zionism, to which the vast majority of Jews in that country adhere."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedman1973246_168-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedman1973246-168">[132]</a></sup>
22.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-171 "Jump up")** Weizmann wrote that: "it appears desirable from every point of view that the British Government should give expression to its sympathy and support of the Zionist claims on Palestine. In fact, it need only confirm the view which eminent and representative members of the Government have many times expressed to us, and which have formed the basis of our negotiations throughout the long period of almost three years"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeizmann1949203_170-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeizmann1949203-170">[133]</a></sup>
23.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-200 "Jump up")** On April 16, 1919, in response to a request from the American Peace Commissioners that he clarify the newspaper report of his views, Wilson stated "Of course I did not use any of the words quoted in the enclosed, and they do not indeed purport to be my words. But I did in substance say what is quoted though the expression "foundation of a Jewish commonwealth" goes a little further than my idea at that time. All that I meant was to corroborate our expressed acquiescence in the position of the British government in regard to the future of Palestine"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETalhami201727_199-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTETalhami201727-199">[159]</a></sup>
24.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-203 "Jump up")** Schmidt cites Stein "Bonar law's views on the Zionist question are unknown" together with his son and his biographer for similar opinions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchmidt201169_202-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchmidt201169-202">[161]</a></sup>
25.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-210 "Jump up")** Sykes' official memorandum providing feedback on the meeting recorded the following:  
    "What the Zionists do not want: I. To have any special political hold on the old city of Jerusalem itself or control over any Christian or Moslem Holy Places; II. To set up a Jewish Republic or any other form of state in Palestine or or in any part of Palestine; III. To enjoy any special rights not enjoyed by other inhabitants of Palestine; On the other hand the Zionists do want: I. Recognition of the Jewish inhabitants of Palestine as a national unit, federated with \[other\] national units in Palestine; II. The recognition of \[the\] right of bona fide Jewish settlers to be included in the Jewish national unit in Palestine"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStrawson200933_209-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStrawson200933-209">[166]</a></sup>
26.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-236 "Jump up")** [Ali Allawi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ali_Allawi "Ali Allawi") explained this as follows: "When Faisal left the meeting with Weizmann to explain his actions to his advisers who were in a nearby suite of offices at the Carlton Hotel, he was met with expressions of shock and disbelief. How could he sign a document that was written by a foreigner in favour of another foreigner in English in a language of which he knew nothing? Faisal replied to his advisers as recorded in ['Awni 'Abd al-Hadi's](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Awni_Abd_al-Hadi "Awni Abd al-Hadi") memoirs, "You are right to be surprised that I signed such an agreement written in English. But I warrant you that your surprise will disappear when I tell you that I did not sign the agreement before I stipulated in writing that my agreement to sign it was conditional on the acceptance by the British government of a previous note that I had presented to the Foreign Office… \[This note\] contained the demand for the independence of the Arab lands in Asia, starting from a line that begins in the north at Alexandretta-Diyarbakir and reaching the Indian Ocean in the south. And Palestine, as you know, is within these boundaries… I confirmed in this agreement before signing that I am not responsible for the implementation of anything in the agreement if any modification to my note is allowed""<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllawi2014189_235-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllawi2014189-235">[187]</a></sup>
27.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-241 "Jump up")** Although it was noted by [UNSCOP](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Special_Committee_on_Palestine "United Nations Special Committee on Palestine") that "To many observers at the time, conclusion of the Feisal-Weizmann Agreement promised well for the future co-operation of Arab and Jew in Palestine."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUNSCOP1947II,_Art._122_239-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUNSCOP1947II,_Art._122-239">[190]</a></sup> and further referring to the 1937 report of the Palestine Royal Commission which noted that "Not once since 1919 had any Arab leader said that co-operation with the Jews was even possible" despite expressed hopes to the contrary by British and Zionist representatives.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalestine_Royal_Commission193778_240-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalestine_Royal_Commission193778-240">[191]</a></sup>
28.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-245 "Jump up")** Ce sentiment de respect pour les autres religions dicte mon opinion touchant la Palestine, notre voisine. Que les juifs malheureux viennent s'y refugieret se comportent en bons citoyens de ce pays, notre humanite s'en rejouit mais quells soient places sous un gouverment musulman ou chretien mandate par La Societe des nations. S'ils veulent constituer un Etat et revendiquer des droits souveraigns dans cette region je prevois de tres graves dangers. Il est a craindre qu'il y ait conflit entre eux et les autres races.
29.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-250 "Jump up")** Lloyd George stated in his testimony to the Palestine Royal Commission: "The idea was, and this was the interpretation put upon it at the time, that a Jewish State was not to be set up immediately by the Peace Treaty without reference to the wishes of the majority of the inhabitants. On the other hand, it was contemplated that when the time arrived for according representative institutions to Palestine, if the Jews had meanwhile responded to the opportunity afforded them by the idea of a national home and had become a definite majority of the inhabitants, then Palestine would thus become a Jewish Commonwealth."<sup id="cite_ref-Peel23_249-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-Peel23-249">[198]</a></sup>
30.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-252 "Jump up")** Amery's testimony under oath to the [Anglo-American Committee of Inquiry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anglo-American_Committee_of_Inquiry "Anglo-American Committee of Inquiry") in January 1946: "The phrase "the establishment in Palestine of a National Home for the Jewish people" was intended and understood by all concerned to mean at the time of the Balfour Declaration that Palestine would ultimately become a "Jewish Commonwealth" or a "Jewish State", if only Jews came and settled there in sufficient numbers."<sup id="cite_ref-251"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-251">[199]</a></sup>
31.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-266 "Jump up")** Amery described this moment in his memoirs: "Half an hour before the meeting Milner looked in from his room in the Cabinet offices, next door to mine, told me of the difficulties, and showed me one or two alternative drafts which had been suggested, with none of which he was quite satisfied. Could I draft something which would go a reasonable distance to meeting the objectors, both Jewish and pro-Arab, without impairing the substance of the proposed declaration?"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAmery1953116_265-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAmery1953116-265">[210]</a></sup>
32.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-Storrs43_270-0 "Jump up")** [Ronald Storrs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ronald_Storrs "Ronald Storrs"), Britain's Military Governor of Jerusalem between 1917 and 1920, wrote in 1943: "The Declaration which, in addition to its main Jewish message, was at pains to reassure non-Palestinian Jews on the score of their national status, took no account whatever of the feelings or desires of the actual inhabitants of Palestine. In its drafting, Arabs observed the main and position portion to be reserved for the Jewish people, while the other races and creeds were not so much as named, either as Arabs, Moslems or Christians, but were lumped together under the negative and humiliating definition of "Non-Jewish Communities" and relegated to subordinate provisos. They further remarked a sinister and significant omission. While their religions and civil rights were specifically to be safeguarded, of their political rights there was no mention whatever. Clearly, they had none."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStorrs194351_268-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStorrs194351-268">[212]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHardieHerrman198088_269-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHardieHerrman198088-269">[213]</a></sup>
33.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-Dual_274-0 "Jump up")** The term "twofold duty" was used by the [Permanent Mandates Commission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Permanent_Mandates_Commission "Permanent Mandates Commission") in 1924,<sup id="cite_ref-271"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-271">[214]</a></sup> the phrase "double undertaking" was used by Prime Minister [Ramsay MacDonald](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ramsay_MacDonald "Ramsay MacDonald") in his April 1930 [House of Commons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom "House of Commons of the United Kingdom") speech,<sup id="cite_ref-272"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-272">[215]</a></sup> the [Passfield white paper](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Passfield_white_paper "Passfield white paper"), and his [1931 letter to Chaim Weizmann](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MacDonald_Letter "MacDonald Letter"), whilst the 1937 Palestine Royal Commission used the term "dual obligation".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalestine_Royal_Commission1937218_273-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalestine_Royal_Commission1937218-273">[216]</a></sup>
34.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-276 "Jump up")** At the 9 June 1930 Permanent Mandates Commission, the British Accredited Representative, [Drummond Shiels](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drummond_Shiels "Drummond Shiels"), set out the British policy to reconcile the two communities. The [Permanent Mandates Commission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Permanent_Mandates_Commission_(Palestine) "Permanent Mandates Commission (Palestine)") summarized that "From all these statements two assertions emerge, which should be emphasised: (1) that the obligations laid down by the Mandate in regard to the two sections of the population are of equal weight; (2) that the two obligations imposed on the Mandatory are in no sense irreconcilable. The Mandates Commission has no objection to raise to these two assertions, which, in its view, accurately express what it conceives to be the essence of the Mandate for Palestine and ensure its future." This was quoted in the [Passfield white paper](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Passfield_white_paper "Passfield white paper"), with the note that: "His Majesty's Government are fully in accord with the sense of this pronouncement and it is a source of satisfaction to them that it has been rendered authoritative by the approval of the Council of the League of Nations."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGeddes1991126_275-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGeddes1991126-275">[217]</a></sup>
35.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-278 "Jump up")** 19 February 1919, Balfour wrote to Lloyd George that: "The weak point of our position of course is that in the case of Palestine we deliberately and rightly decline to accept the principle of self-determination. If the present inhabitants were consulted they would unquestionably give an anti-Jewish verdict. Our justification for our policy is that we regard Palestine as being absolutely exceptional; that we consider the question of the Jews outside Palestine as one of world importance, and that we conceive the Jews to have an historic claim to a home in their ancient land; provided that home can be given them without either dispossessing or oppressing the present inhabitants."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedman1973325_277-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedman1973325-277">[218]</a></sup>
36.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-283 "Jump up")** Wilson's January 1918 [Fourteen Points](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fourteen_Points "Fourteen Points") stated a requirement for "free, open-minded, and absolutely impartial adjustment of all colonial claims, based upon a strict observance of the principle that in determining all such questions of sovereignty the interests of the population concerned must have equal weight with the equitable claims of the government whose title is to be determined",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHaiduc-Dale201340_280-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHaiduc-Dale201340-280">[220]</a></sup> McMahon's June 1918 [Declaration to the Seven](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Declaration_to_the_Seven "Declaration to the Seven") stated that "the future government of these regions should be based upon the principle of the [consent of the governed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Consent_of_the_governed "Consent of the governed")",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKhouri1985527_281-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKhouri1985527-281">[221]</a></sup> the November 1918 [Anglo-French Declaration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anglo-French_Declaration "Anglo-French Declaration") stated that the local "national governments and administrations \[will derive\] their authority from the free exercise of the initiative and choice of the indigenous populations,"<sup id="cite_ref-Khouri_101-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-Khouri-101">[80]</a></sup> and the June 1919 [Covenant of the League of Nations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Covenant_of_the_League_of_Nations "Covenant of the League of Nations") stated that "the wishes of these communities must be a principal consideration in the selection of a Mandatory" and described a "sacred trust", which was later interpreted in 1971 by the [International Court of Justice](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice "International Court of Justice") that "the ultimate objective of the sacred trust was the self-determination and independence of the peoples concerned".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDugard2013294_282-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDugard2013294-282">[222]</a></sup>
37.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-Balfour1919q_286-0 "Jump up")** In an August 1919 memo discussing the [Covenant of the League of Nations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Covenant_of_the_League_of_Nations "Covenant of the League of Nations"), Balfour explained: "What I have never been able to understand is how \[our policy\] can be harmonised with the \[Anglo-French\] declaration, the Covenant, or the instructions to the Commission of Enquiry ... In short, so far as Palestine is concerned, the Powers have made no statement of fact which is not admittedly wrong, and no declaration of policy which, at least in the letter, they have not always intended to violate,"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewis2009163_284-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewis2009163-284">[223]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELieshout2016405_285-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTELieshout2016405-285">[224]</a></sup> and further that: "The contradiction between the letter of the Covenant and the policy of the Allies is even more flagrant in the case of the 'independent nation' of Palestine than in that of the 'independent nation' of Syria. For in Palestine we do not propose even to go through the form of consulting the wishes of the present inhabitants of the country, though the [American Commission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/King%E2%80%93Crane_Commission "King–Crane Commission") has been going through the form of asking what they are. The four Great Powers are committed to Zionism. And Zionism, be it right or wrong, good or bad, is rooted in age-long traditions, in present needs, in future hopes, of far profounder import than the desires and prejudices of the 700,000 Arabs who now inhabit that ancient land."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewis2009163_284-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewis2009163-284">[223]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Balfour1919_95-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-Balfour1919-95">[75]</a></sup>
38.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-291 "Jump up")** This statement was first made during a debate regarding the upcoming [centenary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centennial "Centennial") of the Declaration;<sup id="cite_ref-HL2017_289-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-HL2017-289">[227]</a></sup> the Foreign Office subsequently repeated the statement in response to a petition on the [UK Parliament petitions website](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UK_Parliament_petitions_website "UK Parliament petitions website"), which had called for an official apology for the Declaration.<sup id="cite_ref-290"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-290">[228]</a></sup>
39.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-293 "Jump up")** The [United Nations Special Committee on Palestine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Special_Committee_on_Palestine "United Nations Special Committee on Palestine") acknowledged the same in 1947, noting that: "With regard to the principle of self-determination ... it may well be said that the Jewish National Home and the 'sui generis' Mandate for Palestine run counter to that principle."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUNSCOP1947II,_Art._176_292-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUNSCOP1947II,_Art._176-292">[229]</a></sup>
40.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-319 "Jump up")** On walking to the [Hurva Synagogue](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hurva_Synagogue "Hurva Synagogue") on [Shabbat Nachamu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shabbat_Nachamu "Shabbat Nachamu"), Samuel wrote in his memoirs that he "found the surrounding streets densely thronged, and the great building itself packed to the doors and to the roof, mostly by older settlers, some of those who had come to live, and to die, in the Holy City for piety's sake. Now, on that day, for the first time since the destruction of the Temple, they could see one of their own people as governor in the Land of Israel. To them, it seemed that the fulfilment of ancient prophecy might at last be at hand. When, in accordance with the usual ritual, I was 'called to the Reading of the Law' and from the central platform recited in Hebrew the prayer and the blessing, 'Have mercy upon Zion, for it is the home of our life, and save her that is grieved in spirit, speedily, even in our days. Blessed art Thou, O Lord, who makest Zion joyful through her children': and when there followed the opening words of a chapter of Isaiah appointed for that day, 'Comfort ye, comfort ye my people, saith your God. Speak ye comfortably to Jerusalem, and cry unto her, that her warfare is accomplished, that her iniquity is pardoned,' – the emotion that I could not but feel seemed to spread throughout the vast congregation. Many wept. One could almost hear the sigh of generations."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESamuel1945176_318-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTESamuel1945176-318">[252]</a></sup>
41.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-357 "Jump up")** Weizmann explained as follows: "The German government, on the other hand, was deeply distressed that the British government should get the better of it. It called our representatives in Germany together and tried to explain to them that the German government would have eventually done the same thing, but that it could not because of its alliance with Turkey, which compelled it to move slowly in the matter."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPolkehn197589_356-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPolkehn197589-356">[288]</a></sup>
42.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration#cite_ref-360 "Jump up")** In the original German: _Vereinigung jüdischer Organisationen Deutschlands zur Wahrung der Rechte der Juden des Ostens_
